{{short description|Ongoing COVID-19 viral pandemic on cruise ships}}
{{Use dmy dates|date=March 2020}}
{{EngvarB|date=February 2020}}
{{COVID-19 pandemic sidebar|expanded=locations}}

<!-- please do not add excessive references to sars-cov-2 or covid-19 to the lead, as this page is focused on the pandemic on cruise ships, and not the virus or the disease itself.  in addition, the sidebar also has links for the virus and the disease in bold if the user is interested. -->The [[COVID-19 pandemic]] spread to a number of [[cruise ship]]s, with the nature of such ships—including crowded semi-enclosed areas, increased exposure to new environments, and limited medical resources—contributing to the heightened risk and rapid spread of the disease.<ref>{{cite web|first1=Kara |last1=Tardivel |first2=Stefanie B. |last2=White |first3=Krista Kornylo |last3=Duong |url=https://wwwnc.cdc.gov/travel/yellowbook/2020/travel-by-air-land-sea/cruise-ship-travel |title=Cruise Ship Travel – Chapter 8 – 2020 Yellow Book &#124; Travelers' Health &#124; CDC |publisher=C.cdc.gov |date=2019-06-24 |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref>

The British-registered {{ship||Diamond Princess|ship|2}} was the first cruise ship to have a major outbreak on board, with the ship [[quarantine]]d at [[Port of Yokohama|Yokohama]] from 4 February 2020 for approximately one month.  Over 700 people [[COVID-19 pandemic on Diamond Princess|became infected]], and 14 people died. At the time, the ship accounted for over half the reported cases of [[Severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2|SARS-CoV-2]] outside of mainland [[China]].<ref name="theguardian1">{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/live/2020/feb/20/coronavirus-live-updates-diamond-princess-cruise-ship-japan-deaths-latest-news-china-infections |title=Cruise ship accounts for more than half of virus cases outside China – as it happened |newspaper=The Guardian |date=20 February 2020 |accessdate=5 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304102207/https://www.theguardian.com/world/live/2020/feb/20/coronavirus-live-updates-diamond-princess-cruise-ship-japan-deaths-latest-news-china-infections |archive-date=4 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

Governments and ports responded by [[#Docking restrictions|preventing]] many cruise ships from docking and [[#Government travel advisories|advising]] people to avoid travelling on cruise ships.  Similarly, [[#Cruise line suspensions|many cruise lines suspended]] their operations to mitigate the spread of the pandemic.

{{As of|2020|05|02}}, over 40 cruise ships have had [[#Summary of confirmed cases on board|confirmed positive cases]] of coronavirus on board.  The last cruise ship with passengers aboard during the first wave of the pandemic, {{ship|MV|Artania||2}}, docked at its home port with its last eight passengers on 8 June 2020.{{efn|''Arcadia'' had previously docked in Australia, but was required by the Australian government to undock.}}<ref name="final.cnn" /><ref name="guardian.status">{{cite web|first1=Erin |last1=McCormick |first2=Patrick |last2=Greenfield |first3=Uki |last3=Goñi |url=https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2020/apr/09/revealed-6000-passengers-on-cruise-ships-at-sea-despite-coronavirus-crisis |title=Revealed: 6,000 passengers on cruise ships despite coronavirus crisis &#124; World news |newspaper=The Guardian |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref><ref name="newsweek.status">{{cite web|last=Impelli |first=Matthew |url=https://www.newsweek.com/eight-cruise-ships-still-carrying-passengers-sea-coronavirus-cases-grow-around-world-1496034 |title=Eight Cruise Ships Still Carrying Passengers At Sea As Coronavirus Cases Grow Around The World |work=Newsweek |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref><ref name="artania.cbs" /><ref name="deliziosa.gazzettino" /><ref name="artania.phoenix" /><ref name="artania.tricks">{{Cite web|url=https://www.cruisetricks.de/artania-die-letzten-acht-kreuzfahrtschiff-passagiere-sind-zurueck-in-der-heimat/|title=Artania: Die letzten acht Kreuzfahrtschiff-Passagiere sind zurück in der Heimat|date=8 June 2020|website=Cruisetricks.de Kreuzfahrt-Ratgeber|accessdate=3 July 2020}}</ref><ref name="artania.sukf.2">{{Cite web|url=https://www.schiffe-und-kreuzfahrten.de/news/morten-hansen-bringt-die-letzten-8-kreuzfahrtgaeste-nach-hause-ms-artania-in-bremerhaven/205220/|title=Morten Hansen bringt die letzten 8 Kreuzfahrtgäste nach Hause - MS Artania in Bremerhaven|date=8 June 2020|accessdate=3 July 2020}}</ref>  In addition, over 40,000 crew members remained on cruise ships, some in isolation, as of mid-June 2020.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.foxnews.com/travel/at-least-42000-cruise-ship-workers-still-at-sea |title=At least 42,000 cruise ship workers are still trapped at sea: report |date=15 June 2020 |publisher=Fox News|access-date=15 June 2020}}</ref> Many are unable to be [[repatriation|repatriated]] because cruise lines refuse to cover the cost of doing so,<ref name="crew.guardian">{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2020/apr/30/no-end-in-sight-100000-crew-on-cruise-ships-stranded-at-sea-coronavirus |title=Revealed: 100,000 crew never made it off cruise ships amid coronavirus crisis|first1=Erin|last1=McCormick |first2=Patrick|last2=Greenfield |date=30 April 2020|via=www.theguardian.com |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200507114822/https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2020/apr/30/no-end-in-sight-100000-crew-on-cruise-ships-stranded-at-sea-coronavirus |url-status=live |archive-date=2020-05-07}}</ref><ref name="crew.law">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/04/articles/disease/100000-crew-members-stranded-on-cruise-ships-as-cruise-lines-refuse-to-agree-to-pay-for-repatriation-expenses/ |title=100,000 Crew Members Stranded on Cruise Ships as Cruise Lines Refuse to Agree to Pay for Repatriation Expenses|date=30 April 2020|website=Cruise Law News |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200503011243/https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/04/articles/disease/100000-crew-members-stranded-on-cruise-ships-as-cruise-lines-refuse-to-agree-to-pay-for-repatriation-expenses/ |url-status=live |archive-date=2020-05-03}}</ref> and because countries have different and changing rules. The condition is stressful to many employees.<!--some die from non-covid--><ref name=crewstress>{{cite web |title=Nightmare at Sea Ends In Death for Some Cruise Ship Workers |url=https://finance.yahoo.com/news/nightmare-sea-ends-death-cruise-095851490.html |website=finance.yahoo.com |publisher=Bloomberg |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200512181750/https://finance.yahoo.com/news/nightmare-sea-ends-death-cruise-095851490.html |archive-date=2020-05-12 |date=2020-05-12 |url-status=live}}</ref> Multiple suicides have been reported.<ref>{{cite web|title='I Really Need to Go Home': The Cruise Ship Employees Still Stuck at Sea|url=https://www.vice.com/en_us/article/g5pb54/i-really-need-to-go-home-the-cruise-ship-employees-still-stuck-at-sea|last=Yingst|first=Alexandra|date=2020-05-20|website=Vice|language=en|access-date=2020-05-21}}</ref>

== Ships with confirmed cases on board ==
<!-- ordered roughly by date of first known report of first positive case -->

=== ''World Dream'' ===  <!-- 2020.02.03: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:World Dream.jpg|thumb|''World Dream'']]
The cruise ship ''[[World Dream]]'' (registered in the Bahamas, operated by [[Dream Cruises]]) was on a journey from [[Nansha District|Nansha]] Port, Guangzhou, Guangdong, China, to Nha Trang and Da Nang in Vietnam during 19–24 January 2020 with 6,903 persons on board including 108 from Hubei, in which 28 were from Wuhan.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://k.sina.com.cn/article_1644114654_m61ff32de02000wbav.html|title=世界梦号邮轮已有11人确诊 途中最后一夜狂欢视频曝光|publisher=新京报|date=8 February 2020|access-date=19 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200319084334/https://k.sina.com.cn/article_1644114654_m61ff32de02000wbav.html|archive-date=19 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 24 January 2020, the ship returned to Nansha Port. Port customs performed a temperature check for all disembarking passengers and crew, with 31 people sampled and tested for the virus, including those who had fever during the cruise and those who were in close contact with confirmed cases before they boarded for the cruise. All the test results were negative though some of them were later confirmed to be infected.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.bjnews.com.cn/feature/2020/02/07/686085.html|title=危险无人察觉："世界梦号"豪华邮轮疫情始末|publisher=新京报|date=7 February 2020|author=李云蝶|access-date=19 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200331183455/http://www.bjnews.com.cn/feature/2020/02/07/686085.html|archive-date=31 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

Between 24 January 2020 and 2 February 2020, the ship made three additional cruises out of Guangzhou or Hong Kong, including two "cruises to nowhere" and one to the Philippines, although passengers from the journey were not disembarked at Manila due to local resident protests over fear on the virus.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.hk01.com/%E7%AA%81%E7%99%BC/430817/%E6%AD%A6%E6%BC%A2%E8%82%BA%E7%82%8E-%E4%B8%96%E7%95%8C%E5%A4%A2%E8%99%9F%E4%B8%89%E6%AC%A1%E6%97%85%E7%A8%8B%E8%B3%87%E6%96%99%E6%9C%AA%E6%98%8E-%E9%80%B1%E6%9C%AB%E9%81%8A%E8%87%B3%E5%B0%91%E4%B8%89%E5%8D%83%E4%BA%BA%E7%99%BB%E6%B8%AF%E5%B2%B8|title=【武漢肺炎】世界夢號三次旅程資料未明週末遊至少三千人登港岸|publisher=HK01|date=6 February 2020|access-date=19 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200319084337/https://www.hk01.com/%E7%AA%81%E7%99%BC/430817/%E6%AD%A6%E6%BC%A2%E8%82%BA%E7%82%8E-%E4%B8%96%E7%95%8C%E5%A4%A2%E8%99%9F%E4%B8%89%E6%AC%A1%E6%97%85%E7%A8%8B%E8%B3%87%E6%96%99%E6%9C%AA%E6%98%8E-%E9%80%B1%E6%9C%AB%E9%81%8A%E8%87%B3%E5%B0%91%E4%B8%89%E5%8D%83%E4%BA%BA%E7%99%BB%E6%B8%AF%E5%B2%B8|archive-date=19 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

; Confirmed cases <!-- setting this as bold text instead of as a section header to keep the table of contents cleaner -->

On 2 February 2020, the ship departed from Hong Kong for Taiwan with around 3,800 persons on board. On the same night, the cruise company was notified that there were confirmed cases from the ship's former passengers. On the next day, the Guangdong government officially announced that three former passengers from the Vietnam journey had been confirmed infected by the novel coronavirus after they were disembarked. Former passengers from the cruise in China were told to contact local health authority and observer quarantine.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.scmp.com/economy/china-economy/article/3048949/china-scrambles-locate-passengers-cruise-after-least-four|title=China scrambles to locate passengers on cruise after at least four diagnosed with coronavirus|publisher=South China Morning Post|date=4 February 2020|access-date=19 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200224000216/https://www.scmp.com/economy/china-economy/article/3048949/china-scrambles-locate-passengers-cruise-after-least-four|archive-date=24 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

As of 11 February 2020, 12 cases associated with the cruise were confirmed, including 1 ground worker who had temporarily worked on the ship, and 4 relatives of passengers.<ref name=sina2020-02-17>{{cite news|url=https://tech.sina.cn/2020-02-17/detail-iimxxstf2110648.d.html|title="世界梦号"邮轮驶入柬埔寨海域 船员接受新冠病毒筛查|date=17 February 2020|publisher=[[China Radio International|CRI]] online|access-date=19 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200319084326/https://tech.sina.cn/2020-02-17/detail-iimxxstf2110648.d.html|archive-date=19 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

; Quarantine and preventive actions <!-- setting this as bold text instead of as a section header to keep the table of contents cleaner -->

After the Guangdong government official announcement of confirmed cases among former passengers, on 4 February 2020, Taiwan blocked the ship's [[Port#Port of call|port of call]] in [[Kaohsiung]] due to concern on the virus. On 5 February 2020, ''World Dream'' returned to Hong Kong and all 3,800 passengers and crew on board the ship at the time were put under quarantine at [[Kai Tak Cruise Terminal]].<ref name="WashPost_61DPrincess_3exWorldDream">{{cite news | last1= Denyer | first1= Simon | title= Honeymooner among 61 people on cruise ship confirmed as having coronavirus | date= 7 February 2020 |newspaper= [[The Washington Post]] | url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia_pacific/honeymooner-among-61-people-on-cruise-ship-confirmed-as-having-coronavirus/2020/02/07/30a980b4-4961-11ea-8a1f-de1597be6cbc_story.html |access-date=7 February 2020  |archive-url= https://archive.today/20200207164834/https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia_pacific/honeymooner-among-61-people-on-cruise-ship-confirmed-as-having-coronavirus/2020/02/07/30a980b4-4961-11ea-8a1f-de1597be6cbc_story.html |archive-date= 7 February 2020  |url-status=live |url-access =limited}}</ref> The quarantine was lifted on 9 February 2020 after all 1,800 crew members tested negative for the virus. The majority of the passengers were not tested as they had had no contact with the infected Chinese passengers who had been on the ship during 19–24 January.<ref name="World Dream quarantine lifted">{{cite news |title=Passengers leave Hong Kong cruise ship after coronavirus quarantine lifted |url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/world/coronavirus-hong-kong-1.5457471 |access-date=9 February 2020 |publisher=CBC News |date=9 February 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200210000225/https://www.cbc.ca/news/world/coronavirus-hong-kong-1.5457471 |archive-date=10 February 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

; Evacuation of crew members <!-- setting this as bold text instead of as a section header to keep the table of contents cleaner -->

After all passengers were disembarked, ''World Dream'' cruised to Malaysia. The crew were not allowed to leave the ship in several countries, after one passenger who had disembarked tested positive for COVID-19. The ship finally anchored near Bintan Island, Indonesia.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.indozone.id/news/OjsJnB/kisah-kapal-world-dream-sang-petualang-laut-usai-ditolak-bersandar/read-all |title=Kisah Kapal World Dream, Jadi Petualang Laut Usai Ditolak Bersandar |date=21 February 2020}}</ref> The evacuation of 188 Indonesia crew members from the cruise ship was performed by an Indonesian naval hospital ship and all tested negative for COVID-19.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://koran.tempo.co/read/nasional/450518/awak-kapal-world-dream-dibawa-ke-kepulauan-seribu? |title=Awak Kapal World Dream Dibawa ke Kepulauan Seribu |date=27 February 2020}}</ref> On 28 February 2020 they were quarantined for 14 days on the uninhabited [[Sebaru Kecil]] Islet, [[Thousand Islands (Indonesia)|Thousand Islands]], Jakarta.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.thejakartapost.com/news/2020/02/28/jakartas-island-starts-housing-evacuees-from-world-dream-cruise-ship.html |title=Jakarta's island starts housing evacuees from World Dream cruise ship |first=Nina A. |last=Loasana |date=28 February 2020 |access-date=2 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403202531/https://www.thejakartapost.com/news/2020/02/28/jakartas-island-starts-housing-evacuees-from-world-dream-cruise-ship.html |archive-date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.straitstimes.com/asia/se-asia/coronavirus-indonesia-to-bring-back-citizens-aboard-world-dream-cruise-by-naval-ship |title=Coronavirus: Indonesia to evacuate its 188 citizens working on World Dream cruise ship |work=The Straits Times |date=24 February 2020 |access-date=26 February 2020}}</ref>

{{clear}}

=== ''Diamond Princess'' ===  <!-- 2020.02.04: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:Diamond Princess cruising at night, Sakaiminato, Tottori Prefecture, September 2014.jpg|thumb|''Diamond Princess'' in 2014]]
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic on Diamond Princess}}

On 4 February 2020, Japan's [[Ministry of Health, Labour and Welfare]] announced that {{ship||Diamond Princess|ship|2}},{{efn|A cruise ship registered in Britain owned and operated by [[Princess Cruises]] (incorporated in Bermuda and with headquarters in Santa Clarita, California, US), a brand of [[Carnival Corporation & plc]].}} which had docked at [[Port of Yokohama|Yokohama]]{{efn|in [[Tokyo Bay]] near [[Tokyo]]}} the previous day,{{efn|Princess Cruises listed this cruise as a 15-night cruise beginning on 20 January 2020, with arrival in Yokohama scheduled on the 16th day, 4 February 2020, but it had arrived at Yokohama a day early.<ref name="brochure.diamond" /><ref name="ship-diamond-princess" />}} was quarantined at sea with 10 positive cases on board.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.mhlw.go.jp/stf/newpage_09276.html |title=横浜港に寄港したクルーズ船内で確認された新型コロナウイルス感染症について |publisher=Mhlw.go.jp |date=2020-02-05 |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref>

''Diamond Princess'' had originally departed from Yokohama on 20 January 2020 for a roundtrip cruise.{{efn|The cruise (numbered M003), billed as a tour of [[Southeast Asia]] during the [[Lunar New Year]] period, had scheduled stops at [[Kagoshima]] (Japan), [[Hong Kong]] (China), [[Chân Mây Port]]{{efn|near [[Da Nang]] and [[Huế]]}} (Vietnam), [[Hạ Long Bay]]{{efn|a cruise port that serves [[Hanoi]]}} (Vietnam), [[Keelung]]{{efn|near [[Taipei]]}} (Taiwan), and [[Okinawa Prefecture|Okinawa]] (Japan).<ref name="brochure.diamond" />}}<ref name="brochure.diamond">{{cite web |url=https://www.princess.com/html/global/brochures/au/au-aus-asia-2019-2020.pdf |title=Brochure |website=www.princess.com |access-date=2020-04-25 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200424234537/https://www.princess.com/html/global/brochures/au/au-aus-asia-2019-2020.pdf |archive-date=24 April 2020 |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://bnonews.com/index.php/2020/01/timeline-coronavirus-epidemic/|title=Timeline: coronavirus epidemic|access-date=3 March 2020|date=23 January 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200303013717/https://bnonews.com/index.php/2020/01/timeline-coronavirus-epidemic/|archive-date=3 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> On 20 February 2020, the [[World Health Organization]] stated that the ship accounted for more than half of the reported infections around the world outside of China.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Belam|first1=Martin|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/live/2020/feb/20/coronavirus-live-updates-diamond-princess-cruise-ship-japan-deaths-latest-news-china-infections|title=Cruise ship accounts for more than half of virus cases outside China – as it happened|date=2020-02-20|work=The Guardian|access-date=2020-04-14|last2=Quinn|first2=Ben|language=en-GB|issn=0261-3077|last3=Rourke|first3=Alison|last4=Belam|first4=Martin}}</ref>

=== {{anchor|Westerdam|MS Westerdam}} ''Westerdam'' ===  <!-- 2020.02.15: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:Westerdam Nov 24 2015.png|thumb|''Westerdam'' on 24 November 2015]]
In February 2020, the [[Holland America Line]] ship {{ship|MS|Westerdam}}, departing after a stop in Hong Kong on 1 February, was not allowed to call in the Philippines, Japan, and Guam over concerns regarding coronavirus infections.<ref>{{cite web |title=Cruise ship that visited Hong Kong searches for a port after Philippines, Japan deny entry |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/news/2020/02/06/coronavirus-cruise-ship-denied-by-japan-philippines-holland-america/4676988002/ |date=6 February 2020 |website=[[USA Today]] |accessdate=6 February 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200212014728/https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/news/2020/02/06/coronavirus-cruise-ship-denied-by-japan-philippines-holland-america/4676988002/ |archive-date=12 February 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Guam denies entry to ship over coronavirus concerns |first=Jerick |last=Sablan |url=https://www.guampdn.com/story/news/local/2020/02/07/guam-denies-entry-ship-over-coronavirus-concerns/4687803002/ |publisher=[[Pacific Daily News]] |date=7 February 2020 |accessdate=9 February 2020}}</ref> After initially receiving approval on 10 February to let the passengers disembark in Thailand, as the ship was heading to Laem Chabang port near Bangkok, permission to dock was refused the next day. However, the ship was still maintaining its course to Bangkok and at around 10:30&nbsp;am [[Central European Time|CET]] on 11 February, ''Westerdam'' sailed around the southern tip of Vietnam.<ref>{{cite news |title=Thailand bars Westerdam cruise ship, China virus toll tops 1,000 |url=https://www.bangkokpost.com/thailand/general/1855034/thailand-bars-westerdam-cruise-ship-china-virus-toll-tops-1-000 |newspaper=[[Bangkok Post]] |date=11 February 2020 |accessdate=11 February 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Thailand refuses entry to cruise ship with no coronavirus cases |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-health-thailand-cruiseship/thailand-refuses-entry-to-cruise-ship-with-no-coronavirus-cases-idUSKBN20503T?il=0 |accessdate=11 February 2020 |agency=Reuters |date=11 February 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200331183505/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-health-thailand-cruiseship/thailand-refuses-entry-to-cruise-ship-with-no-coronavirus-cases-idUSKBN20503T?il=0 |archive-date=31 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name=":0">{{cite web|url=https://nos.nl/l/2322512|title=Nederlanders vast op cruiseschip Westerdam: 'We hebben behoorlijk spijt'|website=nos.nl|language=nl|access-date=11 February 2020}}</ref> According to Flip Knibbe, a Dutch passenger on the ship, all the passengers had their temperatures checked a second time. Speaking to [[Nederlandse Omroep Stichting|NOS]] on 11 February, Knibbe said "''Dit schip is virusvrij''": 'This ship is virus-free'. Unlike ''Diamond Princess'', those on board were not in quarantine. Everyone could move freely, shops and restaurants were open and the entertainment programme continued.<ref name=":0" />

After ''Westerdam'' was refused at several points of call, on 13 February, the ship was allowed to dock in [[Sihanoukville (city)|Sihanoukville]], Cambodia.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-51484625|title=Cruise ship rejected by five ports docks at last|date=13 February 2020|publisher=BBC News|access-date=13 February 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200213062133/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-51484625|archive-date=13 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> At this point, only the 20 passengers who reported feeling ill were tested, and all of them tested negative.<ref name="auto2">{{cite web|url=https://www.khmertimeskh.com/50691572/health-ministry-asks-malaysia-to-re-test-specimens-of-us-woman-confirmed-positive-for-coronavirus|title=Health Ministry asks Malaysia to re-test specimens of US woman from MS Westerdam confirmed positive for coronavirus|last=Narim|first=Khuon|work=Khmer Times|date=16 February 2020|accessdate=16 February 2020|archive-url=https://archive.today/20200216110208/https://www.khmertimeskh.com/50691572/health-ministry-asks-malaysia-to-re-test-specimens-of-us-woman-confirmed-positive-for-coronavirus|archive-date=16 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="auto1">{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/reuters/2020/02/16/world/asia/16reuters-china-health-cambodia-cruiseship.html|title=Scramble to Track Cambodia Cruise Ship Passengers After Coronavirus Case Reported|last1=Harris|first1=Ebrahim|last2=Sriring|first2=Orathai|last3=Setboonsarng|first3=Chayut|last4=Johnson|first4=Kay|last5=Feast|first5=Lincoln|agency=Reuters|work=The New York Times|date=16 February 2020|accessdate=17 February 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200217074600/https://www.nytimes.com/reuters/2020/02/16/world/asia/16reuters-china-health-cambodia-cruiseship.html|archive-date=17 February 2020|url-status=dead}}</ref>

On 15 February, Malaysia reported that an 83-year-old US citizen who disembarked from ''Westerdam'' and flew into Malaysia on 14 February had tested positive for SARS-CoV-2.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.scmp.com/news/asia/southeast-asia/article/3050814/coronavirus-us-passenger-westerdam-cruise-ship-infected|title=Coronavirus: Westerdam cruise passenger infected, Malaysia confirms|date=15 February 2020|website=South China Morning Post|access-date=15 February 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200215160347/https://www.scmp.com/news/asia/southeast-asia/article/3050814/coronavirus-us-passenger-westerdam-cruise-ship-infected|archive-date=15 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="auto">{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-health-malaysia/american-woman-from-cruise-ship-tests-positive-again-for-coronavirus-in-malaysia-idUSKBN20A06Q|title=American woman from cruise ship tests positive again for Covid-19 in Malaysia|last1=Tostevin|first1=Matthew|last2=Harris|first2=Ebrahim|last3=Ananthalakshmi|first3=A.|last4=Anantharaman|first4=Muralikumar|agency=Reuters|date=16 February 2020|accessdate=16 February 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200216110952/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-health-malaysia/american-woman-from-cruise-ship-tests-positive-again-for-coronavirus-in-malaysia-idUSKBN20A06Q|archive-date=16 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/02/9b8ab0035389-update1-passenger-from-westerdam-confirmed-by-malaysia-to-have-coronavirus.html|title=Passenger from Westerdam confirmed by Malaysia to have coronavirus|agency=Kyodo News|date=16 February 2020|accessdate=16 February 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200216030203/https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/02/9b8ab0035389-update1-passenger-from-westerdam-confirmed-by-malaysia-to-have-coronavirus.html|archive-date=16 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> In a second test, requested by both the [[Holland America Line]] and [[Ministry of Health (Cambodia)|Cambodian authorities]] the woman tested positive again.<ref>{{cite news |title=American Woman from Cruise Ship Tests Positive Again for Coronavirus in Malaysia |url=https://www.nytimes.com/reuters/2020/02/16/world/asia/16reuters-china-health-cambodia-cruiseship.html |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |date=16 February 2020 |accessdate=16 February 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200217074600/https://www.nytimes.com/reuters/2020/02/16/world/asia/16reuters-china-health-cambodia-cruiseship.html |archive-date=17 February 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="auto2"/><ref name="auto1"/><ref name="auto"/><ref>{{cite news|url=https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/02/d4cacae28b40-westerdam-passenger-tests-positive-twice-for-virus-malaysia.html|title=Westerdam passenger tests positive twice for virus: Malaysia|agency=Kyodo News|date=16 February 2020|accessdate=16 February 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200216135011/https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/02/d4cacae28b40-westerdam-passenger-tests-positive-twice-for-virus-malaysia.html|archive-date=16 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Despite these findings, Cambodian Prime Minister [[Hun Sen]] visited the ship, discouraged use of masks, and encouraged the passengers to tour the city, sparking concerns that another spoke was being added to the contagion network.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Beech|first=Hannah|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/02/17/world/asia/coronavirus-westerdam-cambodia-hun-sen.html|title=Cambodia's Coronavirus Complacency May Exact a Global Toll|date=17 February 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=18 February 2020|issn=0362-4331|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200218010645/https://www.nytimes.com/2020/02/17/world/asia/coronavirus-westerdam-cambodia-hun-sen.html|archive-date=18 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Further cruise passengers were denied entry to Malaysia from Cambodia as a result.{{citation needed|date=March 2020}}

On 22 February, after treatment with antiviral medications that were speculated to have an effect against COVID-19, the woman's medical condition improved and she was tested negative for SARS-CoV-2. The United States [[Centers for Disease Control and Prevention]] (CDC) initially stated that the woman had never been infected by SARS-CoV-2, but withdrew the claim, clarifying that the CDC "[has] no visibility on whether the initial test of the woman was anything other than positive".<ref name="USA_Today_Westerdam_woman">{{cite news | last1= Hines | first1= Morgan | last2= Mandell | first2= Andrea | title= Westerdam cruise ship passenger now negative for coronavirus | date= 25 February 2020 |newspaper= [[USA Today]] | url= https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/02/21/coronavirus-holland-america-ms-westerdam-cruise-passenger-cleared/4834124002/ |accessdate=25 February 2020 |archive-url= https://archive.today/20200225103203/https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/02/21/coronavirus-holland-america-ms-westerdam-cruise-passenger-cleared/4834124002/ |archive-date= 25 February 2020 |url-status=live}}</ref> Due to possible background politics, it is uncertain whether these results were a false negative,<ref name=Time-5789745>{{cite news |url= https://time.com/5789745/westerdam-coronavirus-false-positive/ |title= An American Westerdam Cruise Ship Passenger Does Not Have COVID-19 |work= Time |first= Jaime |last= Ducharme |date= 24 February 2020 |access-date= 3 March 2020 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200228030236/https://time.com/5789745/westerdam-coronavirus-false-positive/ |archive-date= 28 February 2020 |url-status= live }}</ref> or whether the passenger cleared the virus from her system after 72 hours of intensive treatment.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2020/02/22/health-ministry-explains-american-covid-19-patient-recovering-after-treatme/1839855|title=Health Ministry explains American Covid-19 patient recovering after treatment, after US, Cambodia insist she wasn't infected at all|last=Ar|first=Zurairi|work=The Malay Mail|date=22 February 2020|accessdate=23 February 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200223040751/https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2020/02/22/health-ministry-explains-american-covid-19-patient-recovering-after-treatme/1839855|archive-date=23 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== ''Grand Princess'' ===  <!-- 2020.03.04: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically --><!-- note: reports as early as 2020.03.02 did not name the ship -->
{{main|COVID-19 pandemic on Grand Princess}}
[[File:Grand Princess (ship, 1998) IMO 9104005, in Split, 2011-10-13.jpg|thumb|''Grand Princess'' in [[Split, Croatia]], 2011]]
<!-- [[File:Maryland National Guard (49676182507).jpg|thumb|A member of the [[Maryland National Guard]] before transporting passengers from ''Grand Princess'']] -->
[[File:California National Guard's 129th Rescue Wing delivering Covid-19 test-kits to the Grand Princess Cruise liner DOD 107714355-5e6fb4b0cca35.webm|thumb|[[California National Guard]]'s [[129th Rescue Wing]] airlifting test kits to ''Grand Princess''|thumbtime=0]]
Public health officials from [[Placer County, California|Placer County]], [[California]], U.S., reported that an elderly resident with underlying health conditions who had died{{efn|This marked the first death known at the time in California attributable to the virus.<ref name=":8">{{cite press release|author=<!-- No byline -->|title=Placer County Confirms Second Case of COVID-19; Declares Local Health Emergency to Ensure Adequate Resources|url=https://www.placer.ca.gov/6437/Placer-County-confirms-second-case-of-CO|agency=[[Placer County, California]]|date=4 March 2020|access-date=4 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304070536/https://www.placer.ca.gov/6437/Placer-County-confirms-second-case-of-CO|archive-date=4 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=":9">{{cite press release|author=<!-- No byline -->|title=Death of Patient with COVID-19|url=https://www.placer.ca.gov/6438/Death-of-patient-with-COVID-19|agency=[[Placer County, California]]|date=4 March 2020|access-date=4 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200305022748/https://www.placer.ca.gov/6438/Death-of-patient-with-COVID-19|archive-date=5 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>  It would be discovered on 2020.04.21 that a 57-year-old woman from [[San Jose, California|San Jose]] had died on 2020.02.06 from the virus.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.sccgov.org/sites/covid19/Pages/press-release-04-21-20-early.aspx|title=County of Santa Clara Identifies Three Additional Early COVID-19 Deaths – Novel Coronavirus (COVID-19) – County of Santa Clara|website=www.sccgov.org}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.sfchronicle.com/health/article/San-Jose-woman-who-died-Feb-6-showed-no-symptoms-15222877.php|title=San Jose woman who died Feb. 6 showed no symptoms of coronavirus, father says|date=24 April 2020|website=SFChronicle.com}}</ref>}} on 4 March 2020 had tested positive for SARS-CoV-2 after returning from a [[Mexican Riviera]]{{efn|The 10-day cruise sailed from San Francisco to Mexico and back, making four stops in Mexico, as noted in [[COVID-19 pandemic on Grand Princess#Itinerary|the itinerary]].}} cruise on {{ship||Grand Princess}} between 11 and 21 February.<ref name="press.democrat.1">{{cite web|url=https://www.pressdemocrat.com/news/10784064-181/first-coronavirus-death-in-california|title=Locals on same cruise ship as man who died from coronavirus concerned about spread|date=5 March 2020|website=Santa Rosa Press Democrat|access-date=7 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200307011343/https://www.pressdemocrat.com/news/10784064-181/first-coronavirus-death-in-california|archive-date=7 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=sun>{{cite web |url=https://eu.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/04/coronavirus-princess-cruises-ship-met-protest-over-no-testing/4950651002/ |title=Coronavirus: Californian who died likely got it on Princess Cruise |newspaper=[[USA Today]] |date=4 March 2020 |first=Morgan |last=Hines |access-date=4 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200305192959/https://eu.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/04/coronavirus-princess-cruises-ship-met-protest-over-no-testing/4950651002/ |archive-date=5 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|date=4 March 2020|access-date=4 March 2020|title=Placer County reports 2nd coronavirus case. 'Critically ill' patient was on cruise ship|last=Yoon-Hendricks|first=Alexandra|url=https://www.sacbee.com/news/local/article240871226.html|work=[[The Sacramento Bee]]}}</ref>

As a result of increasing reports of former passengers of ''Grand Princess'' testing positive, Princess Cruises, the owner and operator of ''Grand Princess'', working with the [[Centers for Disease Control and Prevention]] (CDC), the government of California, and public health officials in San Francisco, terminated a port call in [[Ensenada, Baja California|Ensenada]], Mexico, planned for 5 March and ordered the ship to return to San Francisco over concerns about the potential for an outbreak on board.<ref name="usa.today.1" />  Some passengers{{efn|These were the 62 passengers that were also on the previous cruise to Mexico.<ref name="usa.today.1" />}} were quarantined in their own on-board staterooms on 4 March by order of the CDC.<ref name="usa.today.1">{{cite web|date=4 March 2020|access-date=5 March 2020|title=Thousands may have been exposed to coronavirus on Princess cruise ship; 62 passengers confined|last1=Hines|first1=Morgan|work=[[USA Today]]|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/04/coronavirus-princess-cruises-ship-met-protest-over-no-testing/4950651002/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200305030815/https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/04/coronavirus-princess-cruises-ship-met-protest-over-no-testing/4950651002/|archive-date=5 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>  In addition, out of the 3533 people on board the ship (2422 passengers and 1111 crew members),<ref name="princess.1">{{cite web |title= Grand Princess Updates & Health Advisory |publisher= Princess Cruise Lines |url= https://www.princess.com/news/notices_and_advisories/notices/grand-princess-updates.html |access-date= 5 March 2020 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200304221115/https://www.princess.com/news/notices_and_advisories/notices/grand-princess-updates.html |archive-date= 4 March 2020 |url-status= live }}</ref> 11 passengers and 10 crew members were exhibiting potential symptoms, and ''Grand Princess'' was ordered by the government of California to remain offshore while the [[California National Guard]]'s [[129th Rescue Wing]] airlifted test kits by helicopter to the ship.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/04/world/coronavirus-news.html|title=Cruise Ship Held Off California Becomes New Focus of Concern|date=6 March 2020|via=NYTimes.com|access-date=5 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304052003/https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/04/world/coronavirus-news.html|archive-date=4 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|date=4 March 2020|access-date=5 March 2020|title=Princess Cruises ship held up off California coast with sick passengers, awaiting coronavirus tests|last=Simpson|first=Hannah|work=[[The Washington Post]]|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/travel/2020/03/04/princess-cruises-ship-held-up-off-california-coast-awaiting-coronavirus-tests/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200305112533/https://www.washingtonpost.com/travel/2020/03/04/princess-cruises-ship-held-up-off-california-coast-awaiting-coronavirus-tests/|archive-date=5 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.militarytimes.com/video/2020/03/06/see-air-national-guard-members-board-a-cruise-ship-with-coronavirus-test-kits-newsbreak/|title=See Air National Guard members board a cruise ship with coronavirus test kits &#124; Newsbreak|website=Military Times|access-date=6 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200309212758/https://www.militarytimes.com/video/2020/03/06/see-air-national-guard-members-board-a-cruise-ship-with-coronavirus-test-kits-newsbreak/|archive-date=9 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 6 March, [[Vice President of the United States|U.S. Vice President]] [[Mike Pence]] announced that, of the 46 tests conducted, 19 crew members and 2 passengers had tested positive,<ref name="task.force.briefing.1" /> and added that the ship would be brought to a non-commercial port, with everyone on the ship being tested and quarantined as necessary,<ref name="task.force.briefing.1">{{cite web |url= https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pAsq7-_3XTI |title= Vice President Pence and Members of the Coronavirus Task Force Hold a Press Briefing |date= 6 March 2020 |first1= Mike |last1= Pence |publisher= Youtube |work= The White House |access-date= 6 March 2020 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200306205750/https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pAsq7-_3XTI&app=desktop |archive-date= 6 March 2020 |url-status= live }}</ref> while [[Donald Trump|President Trump]], ignoring expert advice, wanted those on board ''Grand Princess'' to stay on the ship so that they would not be counted as American cases, which would otherwise "double because of one ship that wasn't our fault".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-keep-passengers-on-grand-princess-cruise-ship-coronavirus-2020-3|title=Trump wants to keep people on coronavirus-hit Grand Princess cruise ship|website=Business Insider|date=7 March 2020|first=Morgan|last=McFall-Johnsen|access-date=7 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200307123701/https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-keep-passengers-on-grand-princess-cruise-ship-coronavirus-2020-3|archive-date=7 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 9 March, the ship docked at the [[Port of Oakland]] and passengers started disembarking.<ref>{{cite web |title=Coronavirus-Stricken Grand Princess Arrives At Port Of Oakland; Passenger Says 'It Looks Like A War Zone' |url=https://sanfrancisco.cbslocal.com/2020/03/09/coronavirus-stricken-grand-princess-golden-gate-bridge-sick-passengers-oakland/ |accessdate=10 March 2020 |date=9 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200310004559/https://sanfrancisco.cbslocal.com/2020/03/09/coronavirus-stricken-grand-princess-golden-gate-bridge-sick-passengers-oakland/ |archive-date=10 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> More than 3,000 people on board were to be quarantined, with passengers at land facilities and the crew on board.<ref name=WP202010th>{{cite web |last1=Albergotti |first1=Reed |title=Grand Princess cruise ship carrying coronavirus patients docks in Oakland |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/nation/2020/03/09/grand-princess-cruise-ship-infected-with-coronavirus-docks-oakland/ |website=Washington Post |accessdate=10 March 2020 |language=en |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200310034324/https://www.washingtonpost.com/nation/2020/03/09/grand-princess-cruise-ship-infected-with-coronavirus-docks-oakland/ |archive-date=10 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

By 25 March 2020, the [[United States Department of Health and Human Services|Department of Health and Human Services]] (HHS) said that, of the 1,103 passengers who elected to be tested, 103 tested positive, 699 tested negative, and the remaining results were pending.<ref name="Hines2020-03-25"/>

As of 20 April 2020, neither Princess Cruises, nor the CDC, nor the HHS appeared to have made any subsequent test results public.<ref name="today.1">{{cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/04/20/grand-princess-cruisers-waited-weeks-coronavirus-test-results/5162904002/|title=Some Grand Princess cruise passengers waited weeks for coronavirus test results, or never got tested|first=Curtis|last=Tate|website=USA TODAY}}</ref>  In addition, some passengers complained about waiting for weeks without getting test results back, and some passengers have not been tested at all even though they showed symptoms upon disembarkation, despite Vice President Pence's earlier claim that all passengers would be tested.<ref name="today.1" /><ref name="chronicle.1">{{cite web|url=https://www.sfchronicle.com/bayarea/article/Most-Grand-Princess-passengers-not-tested-for-15141731.php|title=Most Grand Princess passengers in quarantine refused coronavirus tests -often at federal officials' urging|date=19 March 2020|website=SFChronicle.com}}</ref><ref name="post.1">{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/national/grand-princess-passengers-were-quarantined-on-bases-how-many-actually-have-coronavirus-will-remain-a-mystery/2020/03/23/12a91ae4-6bde-11ea-abef-020f086a3fab_story.html|title=Grand Princess passengers were quarantined on bases. How many actually have coronavirus will remain a mystery.|website=Washington Post}}</ref>

The [[COVID-19 pandemic in California|first known person in California]] to die of the virus at the time,<ref name=":9" /> as well as the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Alberta|first cases in Alberta]],<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/edmonton/alberta-reports-first-presumptive-case-of-covid-19-1.5487787|title=Alberta reports 1st presumptive case of COVID-19|date=5 March 2020|website=CBC|access-date=7 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200221134501/https://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/edmonton/alberta-reports-first-presumptive-case-of-covid-19-1.5487787|archive-date=21 February 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> [[COVID-19 pandemic in Hawaii|Hawaii]],<ref name="hawaii.1">{{cite web|url=https://www.khon2.com/coronavirus-2/gov-ige-confirms-first-case-of-coronavirus-in-hawaii/|title=VIDEO: Hawaii resident, passenger aboard Grand Princess confirmed as first coronavirus case in Hawaii|date=7 March 2020|access-date=7 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200307193138/https://www.khon2.com/coronavirus-2/gov-ige-confirms-first-case-of-coronavirus-in-hawaii/|archive-date=7 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> and [[COVID-19 pandemic in Utah|Utah]],<ref name="utah.1">{{cite web |title=Utah Health Officials Announce First Case of COVID-19 – Utah Department of Health |url=https://health.utah.gov/featured-news/utah-health-officials-announce-first-case-of-covid-19 |website=health.utah.gov |access-date=7 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200307191818/https://health.utah.gov/featured-news/utah-health-officials-announce-first-case-of-covid-19 |archive-date=7 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> were all former passengers of ''Grand Princess''.

=== {{Anchor|A Sara|MS A Sara|River Anuket|MS River Anuket|Asara|MS Asara|Anuket|Nile River cruise ship}} ''River Anuket'' ===  <!-- 2020.03.07: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:MS River Anuket R01.jpg|thumb|''River Anuket'' in March 2018]]
{{see also|COVID-19 pandemic in Egypt#Nile River cruise ship}}

A Taiwanese-American tourist, who had been a passenger on a [[Nile River]] cruise ship variously known as {{MS|River Anuket}}<ref name="washington.post.1">{{Cite news |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia_pacific/uae-raises-virus-cases-to-45-new-cases-from-9-nationalities/2020/03/07/52affb1c-6035-11ea-ac50-18701e14e06d_story.html |title= Egypt says cruise ship quarantined over new virus cluster |first1= Maggie |last1= Michael |first2= Samy |last2= Magdy |agency= AP |newspaper= Washington Post |date= 7 March 2020 |access-date= 7 March 2020 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200308193805/https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia_pacific/uae-raises-virus-cases-to-45-new-cases-from-9-nationalities/2020/03/07/52affb1c-6035-11ea-ac50-18701e14e06d_story.html |archive-date= 8 March 2020 |url-status= live }}</ref> or ''Asara'',<ref name="washington.post.2">{{cite news |first1= Sudarsan |last1= Raghavan |first2= Meryl |last2= Kornfield |title= On the Nile, American tourists are among those quarantined on ship hit by coronavirus |newspaper= Washington Post |date= 7 March 2020 |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/on-the-nile-american-tourists-among-those-quarantined-on-ship-hit-by-coronavirus/2020/03/07/51b0f29a-60a1-11ea-ac50-18701e14e06d_story.html |access-date= 8 March 2020 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200308182848/https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/on-the-nile-american-tourists-among-those-quarantined-on-ship-hit-by-coronavirus/2020/03/07/51b0f29a-60a1-11ea-ac50-18701e14e06d_story.html |archive-date= 8 March 2020 |url-status= live }}</ref> discovered that she was positive for SARS-CoV-2 after she returned to [[Taiwan]]. [[World Health Organization]] officials informed Egyptian authorities of the situation, and all crew members and 150 passengers aboard the cruise ship were tested for SARS-CoV-2.<ref name="washington.post.1"/> On 7 March 2020, health authorities announced that 45 people on board had tested positive despite being asymptomatic,<ref name=Twitter1236347954593759232>{{cite tweet|user=DailyNewsEgypt|number=1236347954593759232|date= 7 March 2020 |title=The total number of infected cases from the Nile cruise}}</ref> and that the ship had been placed in quarantine at a dock in [[Luxor]].<ref name="washington.post.1"/>
{{clear}}

=== ''Costa Magica'' === <!-- 2020.03.12: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
On 12 March, two passengers aboard {{ship||Costa Magica}} were reported to be tested positively for COVID-19 while quarantined in [[Martinique]]. The ship, which departed from Guadeloupe with 3,300 people on board, had been disallowed entry at several sea ports including [[Grenada]], [[Tobago]], [[Barbados]] and [[Saint Lucia]], due to the presence of over 300 Italian nationals on board.<ref>{{cite news |title=BREAKING NEWS: Two passengers on ship turned away from St. Lucia test positive for coronavirus |url=https://www.stlucianewsonline.com/breaking-news-two-passengers-on-ship-turned-away-from-st-lucia-test-positive-for-coronavirus/ |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=St. Lucia News Online |date=12 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200322184635/https://www.stlucianewsonline.com/breaking-news-two-passengers-on-ship-turned-away-from-st-lucia-test-positive-for-coronavirus/ |archive-date=22 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

All the passengers were disembarked, and 930 crew members stayed aboard.<ref name="Costa_fox" /> Eventually, the ship stopped {{convert|3|mi|spell=in}} offshore from Miami, and on 26 March, the U.S. Coast Guard reported evacuation of six sick crew members from ''Costa Magica''.<ref name="Costa_nbc">{{cite news |last1=Massarelli |first1=Katelyn |title=Multiple sick crew members on Costa Magica, Costa Favolosa to be evacuated off Miami |url=https://www.nbc-2.com/story/41943042/multiple-sick-crew-members-on-costa-magica-costa-favolosa-to-be-evacuated-off-miami |accessdate=27 March 2020 |work=NBC2 |date=27 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327195430/https://www.nbc-2.com/story/41943042/multiple-sick-crew-members-on-costa-magica-costa-favolosa-to-be-evacuated-off-miami |archive-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="Costa_usatoday">{{cite news |last1=Hines |first1=Morgan |title=Two Costa cruise ships to anchor with sick crew in Miami for 'life-critical' care |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/26/coronavirus-costa-magica-costa-favolosa-miami-sick-crew/2914625001/ |accessdate=27 March 2020 |work=USA Today |date=26 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326231246/https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/26/coronavirus-costa-magica-costa-favolosa-miami-sick-crew/2914625001/ |archive-date=26 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="Costa_fox">{{cite news |last1=Bartiromo |first1=Michael |title=2 Costa cruise ships heading toward Florida with dozens of sick crew members on board |url=https://www.foxnews.com/travel/2-costa-cruise-ships-toward-florida-sick-crew-members |accessdate=27 March 2020 |work=Fox News |date=26 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327002445/https://www.foxnews.com/travel/2-costa-cruise-ships-toward-florida-sick-crew-members |archive-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

=== {{anchor|Braemar|MS Braemar}} ''Braemar'' ===  <!-- 2020.03.13: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:BREAMAR (36487157951).jpg|thumb|{{MS|Braemar||2}} in [[Nieuwe Waterweg]]]]

On 13 March 2020, five passengers tested positive for the COVID-19 virus aboard {{MS|Braemar}}. As a result, the ship was denied entry into its destination, [[the Bahamas]]. The infected patients were discovered after a former passenger of the cruise tested positive in the Canadian province of [[Alberta]]. The infected passenger disembarked off the cruise in [[Kingston, Jamaica]], but it was unknown where they contracted the disease.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.tribune242.com/news/2020/mar/12/breaking-five-bahamas-bound-cruise-ship-test-posit/|title=Cruise Ship Carrying Persons With Coronavirus 'Will Not Be Permitted To Dock'|date=13 March 2020|website=The Tribune|language=en|access-date=13 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327190153/http://www.tribune242.com/news/2020/mar/12/breaking-five-bahamas-bound-cruise-ship-test-posit/|archive-date=27 March 2020|url-status=dead}}</ref>

[[Sint Maarten]] also denied a request from the cruise to allow passengers to fly out.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://thedailyherald.sx/islands/st-maarten-denies-ms-braemar-request-to-allow-passengers-to-fly-out|title=St. Maarten denies 'MS Braemar' request to allow passengers to fly out|date=12 March 2020|website=The Daily Herald|language=en|access-date=13 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200323010158/https://thedailyherald.sx/islands/st-maarten-denies-ms-braemar-request-to-allow-passengers-to-fly-out|archive-date=23 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> [[Cuba]] finally allowed the ship to dock and evacuated all travelers to the [[United Kingdom]] on 17 March.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://abcnews.go.com/US/coronavirus-infected-cruise-ship-stranded-sea-weeks-dock/story?id=69640092 |title=Coronavirus-infected cruise ship stranded at sea for weeks to dock in Cuba |date=17 March 2020 |website=ABC News |language=en |access-date=17 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200317164151/https://abcnews.go.com/US/coronavirus-infected-cruise-ship-stranded-sea-weeks-dock/story?id=69640092 |archive-date=17 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>
{{clear}}

=== ''Costa Luminosa'' === <!-- 2020.03.13: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:Cruise ship Costa Luminosa - 26 June 2010 - (1).jpg|thumb|''Costa Luminosa'' in 2010]]

On 29 February 2020, a 68-year-old Italian man in critical condition was transferred from {{ship||Costa Luminosa}} to a hospital in the [[Cayman Islands]] due to heart issues.<ref name="luminosa.hsa.2" />  On 12 March, the [[Health in the Cayman Islands|Health Services Authority]] of the Cayman Islands announced that the man was their [[COVID-19 pandemic in the Cayman Islands|first confirmed coronavirus case]].<ref name="luminosa.hsa.1">{{cite web|last=Moore |first=Brooke |url=https://www.hsa.ky/public_health/first-case-of-covid-19-in-cayman-islands-confirmed/ |title=First Case of COVID-19 in Cayman Islands Confirmed – Health Services Authority |publisher=Hsa.ky |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="luminosa.herald" />  His death was announced two days later.<ref name="luminosa.hsa.2">{{cite web|last=Moore |first=Brooke |url=https://www.hsa.ky/public_health/government-statement-on-passing-of-covid-19-patient/ |title=Government Statement on Passing of COVID-19 Patient – Health Services Authority |publisher=Hsa.ky |date=14 March 2020 |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref>

On 8 March, a 68-year-old Italian woman was quarantined in the [[Unincorporated territories of the United States|U.S. Territory]] of [[Puerto Rico]] while being tested for the virus. She had arrived there via the ''Costa Luminosa'', a cruise ship that had departed from [[Fort Lauderdale]], [[Florida]], [[United States|U.S.]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nbcmiami.com/news/local/puerto-rico-takes-preventative-measures-for-possible-case-of-covid-19/2202458/|title=Puerto Rico takes Preventative Measures for Possible Case of COVID-19|website=NBC 6 South Florida|language=en-US|access-date=9 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200310151737/https://www.nbcmiami.com/news/local/puerto-rico-takes-preventative-measures-for-possible-case-of-covid-19/2202458/|archive-date=10 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> On 13 March she, her husband and a third person's tests came back positive for the virus, the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico|first confirmed cases in Puerto Rico]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.elnuevodia.com/noticias/locales/nota/trespacientesarrojanpositivoacoronavirusenpuertorico-2552670/ |title=Tres pacientes arrojan positivo a coronavirus en Puerto Rico |language=es |work=elnuevodia.com |date=13 March 2020 |access-date=15 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314173514/https://www.elnuevodia.com/noticias/locales/nota/trespacientesarrojanpositivoacoronavirusenpuertorico-2552670/ |archive-date=14 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 19 March the ship disembarked more than 350 passengers, from the United States and Canada only, at [[Marseille]], France. Buses and then a chartered plane were used to fly them back to Atlanta, Georgia, U.S., without testing for COVID-19. While in flight, the results from those who were tested in Marseille were positive, so those whose results were positive were sat in separated seats. At [[Hartsfield-Jackson Atlanta International Airport]], the passengers were met by people with [[hazmat suit]]s to check their body temperatures, perform visual assessment and ask if any had COVID-19 symptoms. Those without symptoms were to go to customs and then take their baggage. Several of the passengers became positive for COVID-19 later and some of them died.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://edition.cnn.com/2020/04/03/us/costa-luminosa-passengers-ordeal/index.html |title=A Florida man dies days after hundreds of people exposed to coronavirus walked around the world's busiest airport |first1=Faith |last1=Karimi |first2=Dianne |last2=Gallagher |date=3 April 2020 |access-date=3 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403171833/https://edition.cnn.com/2020/04/03/us/costa-luminosa-passengers-ordeal/index.html |archive-date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 23 March there were 36 confirmed cases of COVID-19 out of those who disembarked from the ship.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.ship-technology.com/news/covid-19-costa-luminosa-36-cases/ |title=Covid-19: Authorities confirm 36 coronavirus cases on Costa Luminosa |work=ship-technology.com |date=23 March 2020 |access-date=5 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324155745/https://www.ship-technology.com/news/covid-19-costa-luminosa-36-cases/ |archive-date=24 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 21 March local news in Puerto Rico reported the death of the quarantined Italian woman.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.elnuevodia.com/noticias/locales/nota/fallecelaturistaitalianaquediopositivoacoronavirusenpuertorico-2554666/ |title=Fallece la turista italiana que dio positivo a coronavirus en Puerto Rico |trans-title=Italian tourist who tested positive for coronavirus dies in Puerto Rico |work=elnuevodia.com |language=es |date=22 March 2020 |access-date=22 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200322043327/https://www.elnuevodia.com/noticias/locales/nota/fallecelaturistaitalianaquediopositivoacoronavirusenpuertorico-2554666/ |archive-date=22 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

=== ''Silver Explorer'' === <!-- 2020.03.14: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
{{ship||Silver Explorer}} docked in [[Castro, Chile]], with 111 passengers and 120 crew, after an 83-year-old man fell ill and tested positive for the virus.<ref name="ship-silver-explorer"/><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/world/live-news/coronavirus-outbreak-03-14-20-intl-hnk/h_6d5c274d0fac7faa5deeef41638e325a |title=2 cruise ships are quarantined off Chile's coast |publisher=Cnn.com |date=2020-03-14 |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref>

=== ''Silver Shadow'' === <!-- 2020.03.14: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[Silversea Cruises]] ship {{ship||Silver Shadow|ship|2}} was blocked from disembarking its 608 passengers and crew at the port of [[Recife]] in [[Brazil]], as a 78-year-old Canadian aboard had been suspected of having the virus.<ref>{{cite news |title=Idoso passa mal em cruzeiro, e navio com centenas de pessoas atracado no Recife é isolado por suspeita de coronavírus |url=https://g1.globo.com/pe/pernambuco/noticia/2020/03/12/idoso-passa-mal-em-cruzeiro-e-navio-com-centenas-de-pessoas-ancorado-no-recife-e-isolado-por-suspeita-de-coronavirus.ghtml |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=[[Rede Globo|globo.com]] |date=12 March 2020 |language=pt-br |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200318015329/https://g1.globo.com/pe/pernambuco/noticia/2020/03/12/idoso-passa-mal-em-cruzeiro-e-navio-com-centenas-de-pessoas-ancorado-no-recife-e-isolado-por-suspeita-de-coronavirus.ghtml |archive-date=18 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> Two passengers were later medically disembarked, and one of them tested positive for the virus.<ref name="ship-silver-explorer"/><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/business/tourism-cruises/article241200066.html |title=A Silversea cruise passenger has tested positive for coronavirus in BrazilA Silversea cruise passenger has tested positive for coronavirus in Brazil |website=Miami Herald |date=14 March 2020}}</ref> A Canadian man died of the disease on 26 March. His wife also tested positive for the virus.<ref name="nationalpost-26-03-20">{{cite news |last=Humphreys |first=Adrian |date=2020-03-27 |title=Canadian man dies from COVID-19 in Brazil hospital after being taken off cruise ship |url=https://nationalpost.com/news/canadian-man-dies-from-covid-19-in-brazil-hospital-after-being-taken-off-cruise-ship |work=National Post |publisher=Postmedia Network Inc. |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="globo-26-03-20">{{cite news |date=26 March 2020 |title=Navio que ficou retido por causa do novo coronavírus deixa o Recife depois de 14 dias |url=https://g1.globo.com/pe/pernambuco/noticia/2020/03/26/navio-que-ficou-retido-por-causa-do-novo-coronavirus-deixa-o-recife-depois-de-14-dias.ghtml |work=G1 |publisher=Globo Comunicação e Participações S.A. |trans-title=Ship that was held up because of the novel coronavirus leaves Recife after 14 days |language=pt-br |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref>

=== ''Norwegian Bliss'' === <!-- 2020.03.18: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->

On 18 March 2020, it was reported that [[Norwegian Cruise Line]] had sent a letter to passengers who had booked a cruise{{efn|This refers to the cruise that began on 8 March 2020 and ended on 15 March .<ref name="bliss.news12" />}} on {{ship||Norwegian Bliss}} that "a 2-year-old who traveled aboard the vessel on the 1 March 2020 voyage of the Norwegian Bliss tested positive for COVID-19".<ref name="bliss.news12">[https://newjersey.news12.com/story/41907442/kiyc-several-people-show-covid19-symptoms-after-cruise-they-say-they-wanted-to-reschedule KIYC: Several people show COVID-19 symptoms after cruise they say they wanted to reschedule] New Jersey News 18 March 2020</ref>  Although passengers receiving that letter stated that they wanted to reschedule, Norwegian Cruise Line refused to honor their requests.<ref name="bliss.news12" />  As a result, some people who decided not to embark on the cruise lost thousands of dollars, while others who chose to risk infection by joining the cruise ended up displaying symptoms of the disease while on the cruise.<ref name="bliss.news12" />

=== ''Norwegian Breakaway'' === <!-- 2020.03.19: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->

On 19 March 2020, it was reported that [[Norwegian Cruise Line]] had sent a letter on 18 March to passengers of the {{ship||Norwegian Breakaway}} cruise that began on 7 March and ended on 14 March that someone who had been on the same cruise had tested positive for coronavirus.<ref name="breakaway.wesh">[https://www.wesh.com/article/norwegian-passenger-coronavirus/31790655 Cruise line tells passengers about positive COVID-19 case on ship days after trip ends] Wesh 2 News</ref>  After showing symptoms and being placed in the ship's [[Intensive care unit|ICU]], the guest was taken by ambulance to a hospital at [[Ocho Rios]], [[Jamaica]], during a scheduled stop on 10 March 2020, and was eventually [[medical evacuation|medically evacuated]] to [[Broward Health|Broward Hospital]] in [[Fort Lauderdale, Florida|Fort Lauderdale]], Florida, U.S., on 13 March, where she tested positive on 15 March.<ref name="breakaway.wesh" /><ref name="breakaway.gazette">[https://www.post-gazette.com/news/health/2020/03/24/westmoreland-hempfield-lisa-duffy-coronavirus-cruise-ship-norwegian-test-COVID-positive/stories/202003230140 A cough, a cruise ship and a Westmoreland County case of coronavirus] Pittsburgh Post-Gazette 25 March 2020</ref><ref name="breakaway.herald">[https://www.heraldmailmedia.com/news/special/coronavirus/west-virginia-woman-who-was-on-cruise-with-coronavirus-patient-criticizes-handling-of-situation/article_17ea0a3e-8690-59db-8d74-2fe482fb8b3d.html West Virginia woman who was on cruise with coronavirus patient criticizes handling of situation ] Herald Mail 25 March 2020</ref><ref name="breakaway.itinerary">[https://crew-center.com/norwegian-breakaway-itinerary Norwegian Breakaway Itinerary] Crew Center</ref><ref name="wsj.risk">[https://www.wsj.com/articles/cruise-ships-set-sail-knowing-the-deadly-risk-to-passengers-and-crew-11588346502 Cruise Ships Set Sail Knowing the Deadly Risk to Passengers and Crew] Wall Street Journal</ref>  Many other passengers started showing symptoms but had difficulty getting tested.<ref name="breakaway.wesh" /><ref name="breakaway.gazette" />

Passengers were wondering why the company took so long to inform passengers of the initial positive test, as they had started learning about the result through local news sources and social media instead.<ref name="breakaway.wesh" /><ref name="breakaway.herald" />  Passengers complained that, had they been informed earlier of the test, they could have taken precautions to avoid spreading the virus any further.<ref name="breakaway.wesh" /><ref name="breakaway.wogx">[https://www.wogx.com/news/cruise-passenger-returns-to-florida-home-but-fears-he-may-be-carrying-coronavirus Cruise passenger returns to Florida home but fears he may be carrying coronavirus] Fox 51 19 March 2020</ref>  It was also reported that the disembarkation process was "surprisingly routine", with one former passenger stating that there was "[n]o temperature check, no screenings, no questions asked, nothing", and that he "just walked away from the ship, got on a shuttle and left".<ref name="breakaway.wogx" />

On 24 March 2020, the [[Pittsburgh Post-Gazette]] reported that two former passengers from [[Westmoreland County, Pennsylvania|Westmoreland County]] had tested positive.<ref name="breakaway.gazette" />  At the time, there were 11 confirmed cases in the county.<ref name="breakaway.gazette" />

On 9 April 2020, the passenger who was airlifted to Florida died in isolation at the hospital, after being on a ventilator for nearly 30 days.<ref name="wsj.risk" />

=== ''Celebrity Solstice'' === <!-- 2020.03.20: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->

The [[New Zealand]] [[Ministry of Health (New Zealand)|Ministry of Health]] announced on 20 March 2020 that a man from [[Auckland]] in his 60s that was on {{ship||Celebrity Solstice||2}} had tested positive for the virus.<ref name="nz.health" /> He had boarded the ship in Auckland on 10 March and disembarked at [[Port Chalmers]], a suburb of [[Dunedin]], on 15 March.<ref name="nz.health" /> All New Zealanders on board who returned to New Zealand were considered close contacts and put in isolation.<ref name="nz.health" />

On 23 March 2020, [[Tasmania]]'s [[Department of Health and Human Services (Tasmania)|Department of Health]] reported a positive case who disembarked at [[Sydney]] on 20 March.<ref name="solstice.tas">[https://health.tas.gov.au/news/2020/coronavirus_update_23_march_2020 Coronavirus update – 23 March 2020] Tasmanian Department of Health 23 March 2020</ref>  On 26 March, a man from Perth in his 70s who was a passenger of ''Celebrity Solstice'', died of the disease at [[Joondalup Health Campus]].<ref name="solstice.abc">[https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-26/wa-second-coronavirus-covid-19-death-cruise-ship/12093796 WA records second COVID-19 death after man falls ill following cruise ship holiday] ABC News 27 March 2020</ref>  [[New South Wales]]' [[Ministry of Health (New South Wales)|Ministry of Health]] had reported 11 cases from the ship by 2 April, and 17 cases from the ship as of 9 April.<ref name="nswhealth-2-4-2020"/><ref name="solstice.nsw">[https://www.health.nsw.gov.au/news/Pages/20200409_00.aspx COVID-19 (Coronavirus) statistics] NSW Department of Health 9 April 2020</ref>

The ship left Australia during the weekend of 4 April 2020 with its crew as did four other vessels.<ref name="theguardian2"/>

=== ''Ruby Princess'' === <!-- 2020.03.20: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
{{further |Ruby Princess#2020: spread of COVID-19}} 
[[File:Ruby Princess in Ketchikan.jpg|thumb|''Ruby Princess'' docked in [[Ketchikan, Alaska]] during a 7-day Alaska cruise in August 2019]]
From 15 March 2020, Australia banned cruise ships arriving from foreign ports. However, exemptions were granted to allow four ships, already en route to Australia, to dock and disembark their passengers. On 19 March 2020, {{ship||Ruby Princess}}, which was one of the four ships given the exemption, docked at the [[Overseas Passenger Terminal]] in [[Sydney]], [[Australia]], after a cruise to New Zealand. The cruise ship was forced to return to Sydney early after some passengers reported respiratory problems, but when disembarking passengers were not told that anyone on board presented any symptoms during the voyage.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/world/news/article.cfm?c_id=2&objectid=12321712 |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Ruby Princess mistake caused infection cases to explode |first=Vanessa |last=Brown |date=1 April 2020 |access-date=2 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200402144203/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/world/news/article.cfm?c_id=2&objectid=12321712 |archive-date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 20 March, it was announced that three passengers and a crew member of ''Ruby Princess'' had tested positive for the virus.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.princess.com/news/notices_and_advisories/notices/ruby-princess-advisory.html |title=Ruby Princess Advisory |publisher=Princess Cruises |date=20 March 2020 |access-date=20 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320052806/https://www.princess.com/news/notices_and_advisories/notices/ruby-princess-advisory.html |archive-date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> The ship had docked in [[Port Jackson|Sydney Harbour]], and the passengers had disembarked before the results came back positive.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.9news.com.au/national/coronavirus-four-people-test-positive-for-covid19-after-ruby-princess-cruise/09f9951a-ec5e-4205-9fb8-87a6620ef6b3 |title=Four people test positive for COVID-19 after Ruby Princess cruise |last=Noble |first=Freya |work=9News.com.au |date=20 March 2020 |access-date=20 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320052808/https://www.9news.com.au/national/coronavirus-four-people-test-positive-for-covid19-after-ruby-princess-cruise/09f9951a-ec5e-4205-9fb8-87a6620ef6b3 |archive-date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> The ship had returned to Sydney with 1,100 crew members and 2,700 passengers, and 13 people who were sick were tested for the virus.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.canberratimes.com.au/story/6689361/positive-virus-tests-on-aust-nz-cruise/?cs=14231 |title=Positive virus tests on Aust-NZ cruise |work=The Canberra Times |date=20 March 2020 |access-date=20 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321044017/https://www.canberratimes.com.au/story/6689361/positive-virus-tests-on-aust-nz-cruise/?cs=14231 |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 24 March, one person who was a passenger on the 8–19 March cruise aboard ''Ruby Princess'' died after a coronavirus diagnosis.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.watoday.com.au/national/ruby-princess-passenger-dies-after-coronavirus-diagnosis-20200324-p54ddu.html |title=Ruby Princess passenger dies after coronavirus diagnosis |publisher=WA Today |date=24 March 2020 |access-date=24 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324025057/https://www.watoday.com.au/national/ruby-princess-passenger-dies-after-coronavirus-diagnosis-20200324-p54ddu.html |archive-date=24 March 2020 in Victoria, three in Tasmania and two in the Northern Territory) had tested positive for the virus.<ref name="guardian2020-03-31">{{cite
