}}</ref>
* [[File:The Costa Deliziosa (46733451301).jpg|thumb|''Costa Deliziosa'' in 2018]] {{anchor|Costa Deliziosa}} {{ship||Costa Deliziosa}}: This ship carried 1830 guests and 899 crew and had made a technical call in [[Muscat]], Oman, in early April for food and provisions.<ref name="newsweek.status" />  The company was seeking a port that would allow all of its passengers to disembark.<ref name="newsweek.status" />  Finally, on 18 April, an announcement stated that although French authorities had rejected their docking request, some of the passengers would be disembarking in [[Barcelona]], Spain, and the remaining passengers in [[Genoa]], Italy, during that week.<ref name="deliziosa.bloomberg">{{cite web|url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-04-18/carnival-s-costa-deliziosa-ship-to-let-off-passengers-in-genoa |title=Carnival's Costa Deliziosa Ship to Let Off Passengers in Genoa |publisher=Bloomberg |date=2020-04-18 |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref><ref name="deliziosa.genova24">{{cite web|url=https://www.genova24.it/2020/04/coronavirus-costa-deliziosa-domani-pomeriggio-a-genova-con-2-500-persone-a-bordo-234331/ |title=Coronavirus, Costa Deliziosa oggi pomeriggio a Genova con 2.500 persone a bordo – Genova 24 |publisher=Genova24.it |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref>  As of that time, no cases of COVID-19 had been reported to authorities.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://nymag.com/intelligencer/2020/04/the-last-three-cruise-ships-at-sea-are-finally-going-home.html |title=The Last Three Cruise Ships at Sea Are Finally Going Home|website= New York Magazine |date=20 April 2020}}</ref>  On 20 April 2020, ''Costa Deliziosa'' docked at Barcelona as planned, letting off some of its passengers, including 168 Spanish nationals.<ref name="deliziosa.genova24" />  It then headed off to Genoa, with 1519 passengers and 898 crew members aboard,{{efn|There are conflicting reports on the number of passengers and crew members that headed for Genoa.<ref name="newsweek.status" /><ref name="deliziosa.genova24" /><ref name="deliziosa.gazzettino"/>}} where it docked on 2020.04.22.{{efn|It was scheduled to dock on 2020.04.21, but a storm prevented it from doing so.<ref name="deliziosa.primo" />}}<ref name="deliziosa.genova24" /><ref name="deliziosa.primo">{{cite web|url=https://www.primocanale.it/notizie/genova-deliziosa-all-ingresso-del-porto-il-vento-rallenta-le-operazioni-d-attracco-218565.html |title=Genova, Deliziosa all'ingresso del porto: il vento rallenta le operazioni d'attracco, Genova – Cronaca |publisher=Primocanale.it |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref><ref name="deliziosa.gazzettino">{{cite web|url=https://www.ilgazzettino.it/nordest/venezia/coronavirus_nave_costa_crociera_genova-5186373.html |title=Costa Deliziosa in porto, i crocieristi del giro del mondo rientrati in Italia dopo 108 giorni |publisher=Ilgazzettino.it |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref>  This ship is likely to be the penultimate cruise ship to unload all its passengers during the pandemic, with ''Artania'' being the only ship left with passengers on board at the time ''Costa Deliziosa'' docked.<ref name="final.cnn">{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/travel/article/final-cruise-ships-port/index.html |title=Last cruise ship at sea finally reaches port &#124; CNN Travel |publisher=Cnn.com |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref><ref name="deliziosa.gazzettino" />
* {{ship||Costa Fortuna}}: The Italian cruise ship ''Costa Fortuna'' attempted to dock at [[Phuket Province|Phuket]], [[Thailand]], on 6 March 2020, but was denied by Thai officials because it was carrying passengers who had left Italy within the past two weeks.<ref name="costa.fortuna.1">{{cite web |last1=Corcoran |first1=Kieran |title=An Italian cruise ship was turned away from ports in Malaysia and Thailand even though it has no cases of coronavirus on board |url=https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-costa-fortuna-cruise-ship-denied-by-malaysia-thailand-ports-2020-3 |website=Business Insider |date=7 March 2020 |access-date=7 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200308200609/https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-costa-fortuna-cruise-ship-denied-by-malaysia-thailand-ports-2020-3 |archive-date=8 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 7 March, the ship attempted to dock at [[Penang]] in northern [[Malaysia]], but was denied pursuant to a complete ban on cruise ships.<ref name="costa.fortuna.1" /> The vessel docked in Singapore on 10 March and the passengers disembarked, with some being bused directly to the airport. There were no confirmed cases of COVID-19 aboard the ship.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.channelnewsasia.com/news/singapore/coronavirus-covid-19-costa-fortuna-cruise-dock-12520634 |title=Costa Fortuna cruise ship docks in Singapore; some passengers immediately bussed to airport |work=Channel News Asia |last2=Kit |first2=Tang See |last1=Mahmud |first1=Aqil Haziq |date=10 March 2020 |access-date=25 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200325153759/https://www.channelnewsasia.com/news/singapore/coronavirus-covid-19-costa-fortuna-cruise-dock-12520634 |archive-date=25 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>
* {{ship||Costa neoRomantica}}: On 26 March 2020, the ship with no passengers on board, previously quarantined at [[Nagasaki]], [[Japan]], anchored at the roadstead  of [[Vladivostok]], [[Russia]], to refresh the ship with water, fuel, and food. However, it was denied entrance as the [[Rospotrebnadzor|Russian sanitary officials]] stipulated the dock workers to be quarantined for 14 days. No COVID-19 cases on board were reported.<ref>{{cite news |title=Лайнер Costa Neoromantica прибыл в Приморье на "карантин" |url=https://primpress.ru/article/51980 |accessdate=27 March 2020 |agency=PrimPress |date=26 March 2020 |language=ru |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327190554/https://primpress.ru/article/51980 |archive-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Во Владивостоке лайнеру Costa Neoromantica предложили пройти карантин |url=https://ria.ru/20200326/1569162758.html |accessdate=27 March 2020 |agency=RIA Novosti |date=26 March 2020 |language=ru |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327215010/https://ria.ru/20200326/1569162758.html |archive-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> 
* {{ship||Costa Serena}}: Fifteen passengers aboard ''Costa Serena'' on 24 January were suspected to have SARS-CoV-2.<ref name="serena.safety">{{cite web|url=https://safetyatsea.net/news/2020/cruise-operators-cancel-sailings-from-china-as-coronavirus-outbreak-worsens/|title=Cruise operators cancel sailings from China as coronavirus outbreak worsens – IHS Markit Safety at Sea|website=safetyatsea.net}}</ref>  The ship arrived at its destination, [[Tianjin]], [[China]], on 25 January.<ref name="serena.safety" />  Quarantine officials boarded the ship to screen all passengers and crew member, and found 17 people with fevers.<ref name="serena.safety" /><!-- unsourced information -- 146 (of 3,706) passengers from [[Hubei province]] where the disease originated, an emergency was declared.  The cruise ship was locked down for 19 hours -->  All tests returned negative later that day, and everyone was ordered to disembark and have their photographs and temperatures taken as an additional precaution.<ref name="serena.safety" />
* {{ship||Costa Smeralda|ship|2}}: In January, ''Costa Smeralda'' and her 6,000 passengers were quarantined at the port of [[Civitavecchia]] in [[Rome]], [[Italy]], following two suspected cases.<ref name="corona">{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/jan/30/6000-passengers-stuck-on-cruise-ship-in-italy-over-coronavirus-fears |title=6,000 passengers stuck on cruise ship in Italy over coronavirus fears |website=theguardian.com |accessdate=30 January 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200130145634/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/jan/30/6000-passengers-stuck-on-cruise-ship-in-italy-over-coronavirus-fears |archive-date=30 January 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> A spokesperson from Costa Cruises stated that a 54-year-old woman aboard the ship was suffering from a fever and that she and her husband were both being tested. They were found to be uninfected, and passengers were allowed to go on shore the next day.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/01/30/asia/wuhan-coronavirus-update-china-spread-intl-hnk/index.html|title=7,000 held on cruise ship in Italy as global fears spread over coronavirus|first1=James|last1=Griffiths|first2=Angela|last2=Dewan|first3=Gianluca|last3=Mezzofiore|first4=Livia|last4=Borghese|website=CNN|access-date=30 January 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200130111950/https://www.cnn.com/2020/01/30/asia/wuhan-coronavirus-update-china-spread-intl-hnk/index.html|archive-date=30 January 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>
* {{ship||Emerald Princess}}: Reports in May 2020 indicated that there had been no confirmed COVID-19 cases on this vessel<ref name="abc7.com">{{cite web|url=https://abc7.com/6164841/|title=Stuck at sea: Tens of thousands of cruise ship workers still adrift amid coronavirus pandemic|first1=Phillip|last1=Palmer|first2=Lisa|last2=Bartley|date=9 May 2020|website=ABC7 Los Angeles}}</ref> which was docked in Florida as of 9 May 2020. Some days earlier, it had been denied permission to dock at [[Nassau, Bahamas|Nassau]], but by that time, contained only crew members.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://winnipeg.citynews.ca/2020/05/09/canadians-who-work-on-two-cruise-ships-are-being-allowed-off-in-u-s-ports/|title=Canadians who work on two cruise ships are being allowed off in U.S. ports|date=9 May 2020}}</ref> Passengers had been allowed to disembark previously. On 9 May, the 123 Canadian and American crew members<ref>{{cite web|url=https://miami.cbslocal.com/2020/05/09/emerald-princess-crew-members-port-everglades/|title=US, Canadian Emerald Princess Crew Members Disembark At Port Everglades|date=9 May 2020}}</ref> were allowed to disembark at [[Port Everglades]], although others remained on board.<ref name="abc7.com"/>
* {{MS|Europa|1999|2}}: The ship docked in [[Puerto Vallarta]], Mexico. The government announced on 25 March that it would receive cruise ships "for humanitarian reasons," but that passengers would be individually "fumigated" before being taken directly to airports to be returned to their home countries. The protocol would apply to ''Europa'' and other ships in Mexican waters.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://apnews.com/01aea6b6217f0464be47180c27af389f |title=Mexico will receive cruise ships, but fumigate passengers |agency=Associated Press |date=25 March 2020 |access-date=29 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200328225325/https://apnews.com/01aea6b6217f0464be47180c27af389f |archive-date=28 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>
* {{ship||Grandeur of the Seas}}: On 12 March 2020, ''Grandeur of the Seas'' was denied a request to berth at the [[Transportation in the United States Virgin Islands#Cruise ships|Austin "Babe" Monsanto Marine Terminal]] in the [[United States Virgin Islands]] because a crew member had  travelled to Japan within the previous two weeks, even though no confirmed cases of coronavirus were on board.<ref name="vipa">{{cite web |url=https://doh.vi.gov/news/vipa-confirms-coast-guard-denied-entry-grandeur-seas-cruise-ship |title=VIPA Confirms That Coast Guard Denied Entry To Grandeur Of The Seas Cruise Ship |publisher=United States Virgin Islands Department of Health |date=13 March 2020 |access-date=21 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200315192801/https://doh.vi.gov/news/vipa-confirms-coast-guard-denied-entry-grandeur-seas-cruise-ship |archive-date=15 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cruiseindustrynews.com/cruise-news/22587-virgin-islands-deny-grandeur-of-the-seas-call.html |title=Virgin Islands Deny Grandeur of the Seas Call |work=Cruise Industry News |date=12 March 2020 |access-date=21 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321222945/https://www.cruiseindustrynews.com/cruise-news/22587-virgin-islands-deny-grandeur-of-the-seas-call.html |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>  The ship, however, was eventually allowed to return to transport a seriously-injured passenger to a hospital for treatment.<ref name="vipa" />
* {{anchor|Jewel of the Seas}} {{ship||Jewel of the Seas}}:
** On 2020.03.11, two passengers aboard ''Jewel of the Seas'' were experiencing respiratory illnesses while the ship was docked at the [[Mina Rashid|Dubai Cruise Terminal]].{{efn|Both passengers were diagnosed with symptoms unrelated to the coronavirus.<ref name="jewel.arabia.1" />}}<ref name="jewel.arabia.1">{{cite web|url=https://cruisearabiaonline.com/2020/03/11/royal-caribbeans-jewel-of-the-seas-returns-to-dubai-after-passengers-develop-respiratory-symptoms/|title=Royal Caribbean's Jewel of the Seas returns to Dubai after passengers develop respiratory symptoms|first=Shaun|last=Ebelthite|date=11 March 2020|website=cruisearabiaonline.com}}</ref><ref name="jewel.hive">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruisehive.com/royal-caribbean-ship-cancels-cruise-after-covid-19-tests/38331|title=Royal Caribbean Ship Cancels Cruise After COVID-19 Tests|date=12 March 2020}}</ref>  After the ship was placed in quarantine, test results for the two sick passengers returned negative, and the ship was given the all clear.{{efn|''Business Insider'' reported that the two passengers had tested positive, while inexplicably linking to an article that said they had tested negative.<ref name="jewel.insider">{{cite web|url=https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-royal-caribbean-cruise-cruises-next-30-days-2020-3|title=Royal Caribbean is halting new cruises for the next 30 days in the US amid coronavirus threat|first=Rachel|last=Premack|website=Business Insider}}</ref>}}<ref name="jewel.arabia.2">{{cite web|url=https://cruisearabiaonline.com/2020/03/12/royal-caribbean-ship-jewel-of-the-seas-gets-all-clear-after-coronavirus-scare-in-dubai/|title=Royal Caribbean ship Jewel of the Seas gets all clear after Coronavirus scare in Dubai|first=Shaun|last=Ebelthite|date=12 March 2020|website=cruisearabiaonline.com}}</ref>  However, because many ports had begun to close, ''Jewel of the Seas'' ended up staying at Dubai for the duration of the cruise, and Royal Caribbean gave the passengers full refunds and allowed them to use the ship as a hotel.<ref name="jewel.arabia.2" /><ref name="jewel.hive" />
** On 2020.04.29, a 27-year-old male Polish electrician of ''Jewel of the Seas'' jumped overboard from deck 12 while the ship was anchored near [[Corfu]], Greece.<ref name="jewel.pireas">{{Cite web|url=http://www.pireasnews.gr/2020/05/jewel-of-seas-27-48.html|title=Τι έδειξαν οι κάμερες του Jewel of the Seas για τον 27χρονο ναυτικό - 48 ώρες αργότερα κατάλαβαν την απουσία του|accessdate=3 July 2020}}</ref><ref name="jewel.law">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/05/articles/disappearances/crew-member-goes-overboard-from-jewel-of-the-seas/|title=Crew Member Goes Overboard from Jewel of the Seas|date=3 May 2020|website=Cruise Law News}}</ref><ref name="jewel.mapper">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruisemapper.com/accidents/Jewel-Of-The-Seas-569|title=Jewel Of The Seas accidents and incidents|website=CruiseMapper}}</ref><ref name="jewel.crew">{{cite web|url=https://crew-center.com/crew-member-goes-overboard-jewel-seas|title=Crew Member Goes Overboard from Jewel of the Seas &#124; Crew Center|website=crew-center.com}}</ref>  His absence was only realized over two days later.<ref name="jewel.pireas" />  The [[Hellenic Coast Guard]] conducted a large search operation but was unsuccessful.<ref name="jewel.pireas" />
* {{ship|MS|Maasdam||2}}: 842 guests and 542 crew members from Holland America Line's ''Maasdam'' were not allowed to disembark in [[Honolulu]] on 19 March 2020.<ref name=honolulu>{{cite web |url=https://news.yahoo.com/despite-no-reported-coronavirus-hawaii-wont-let-cruise-155328921--abc-news-topstories.html |title=Despite no reported coronavirus, Hawaii won't let cruise ship passengers disembark |first=Christina |last=Carrega |work=ABC News |date=19 March 2020 |access-date=20 March 2020 |via=Yahoo News |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320214237/https://news.yahoo.com/despite-no-reported-coronavirus-hawaii-wont-let-cruise-155328921--abc-news-topstories.html |archive-date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>
* {{MS|Marco Polo||2}}: Kenyan authorities screened passengers on ''Marco Polo'' for coronavirus when the cruise ship docked at [[Mombasa]] on 13 February 2020.<ref>{{cite news | title= Cruise ship docks in Mombasa, passengers cleared of coronavirus | url= https://www.kbc.co.ke/cruise-ship-docks-in-mombasa-passengers-cleared-of-coronavirus/ | work= KBC Channel | publisher= Kenya Broadcasting Corporation | date= 13 February 2020 | agency= Kenya News Agency | access-date= 30 March 2020 | quote= The Port of Mombasa Thursday morning welcomed a cruise ship christened 'Ms Marco Polo with 575 passengers and 346 crew members on board. [...] Kenya Ports Authority managing director Daniel Manduku [...] said that the port health department has taken measures to screen all passengers before disembarking from the ship in order to avert entry of diseases such as coronavirus which has greatly affected China. | archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200214180454/https://www.kbc.co.ke/cruise-ship-docks-in-mombasa-passengers-cleared-of-coronavirus/ | archive-date= 14 February 2020 | url-status= live }}</ref>
* {{anchor|Mariner of the Seas}} {{ship||Mariner of the Seas}}: On 10 May 2020, a male Chinese crew member of ''Mariner of the Seas'' was found dead aboard the ship.<ref name="mariner.law">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/05/articles/disease/crew-member-found-dead-on-the-mariner-of-the-seas/|title=Crew Member Found Dead on the Mariner of the Seas|date=11 May 2020|website=Cruise Law News}}</ref>{{efn|''Schiffe und Kreuzfahrten'' reported that ''Cruise Law News'' had stated that the crew member was found dead in his cabin, although the article ''Cruise Law News'' published appeared to not include this detail.<ref name="mariner.sukf">{{cite web|url=https://www.schiffe-und-kreuzfahrten.de/news/mariner-of-the-seas-crewmitglied-tot-in-seiner-kabine-gefunden/203807/|title=Mariner of the Seas: Crewmitglied Tot in seiner Kabine gefunden|date=11 May 2020}}</ref><ref name="mariner.law" />}}  The ship is owned by [[Royal Caribbean Cruises Ltd.|Royal Caribbean Cruises]], which, according to the ''[[Miami Herald]]'', has refused to repatriate many crew members due to the associated costs, with many crew members turning to desperate measures, such as [[hunger strike]]s, as a result.<ref name="herald.royal.1">{{cite web | last=Dolven | first=Taylor | title=Cruise companies refuse CDC terms to repatriate crew, call transport 'too expensive' | website=miamiherald | date=2020-04-30 | url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/business/tourism-cruises/article242380421.html | access-date=2020-05-23}}</ref><ref name="herald.royal.5">{{cite web | last1=Ocasio | first1=Bianca Padró | last2=Dolven | first2=Taylor | title=Desperate cruise employees say they're losing hope amid reports of overboard deaths | website=miamiherald | date=2020-05-10 | url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/business/tourism-cruises/article242638061.html | access-date=2020-05-23}}</ref>
* {{ship||MSC Meraviglia}}: On 26 February, [[COVID-19 pandemic in Mexico|Mexican]] authorities granted permission for ''MSC Meraviglia'', registered in [[Malta]], to dock in [[Cozumel]], Quintana Roo, because she carried a passenger presumed to be infected with the [[COVID-19 pandemic|coronavirus]]. The ship was previously denied access to ports in [[COVID-19 pandemic in Jamaica|Jamaica]] and the [[COVID-19 pandemic in the Cayman Islands|Cayman Islands]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.eluniversal.com.mx/english/msc-meraviglia-cruise-ship-dock-cozumel-mexico-despite-coronavirus-fears |title=MSC Meraviglia cruise ship to dock in Cozumel, Mexico despite coronavirus fears |work=El Universal (English) |date=26 February 2020 |access-date=15 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314023755/https://www.eluniversal.com.mx/english/msc-meraviglia-cruise-ship-dock-cozumel-mexico-despite-coronavirus-fears |archive-date=14 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> Two cases of common seasonal flu were found.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.maritime-executive.com/article/mexico-no-coronavirus-on-msc-meraviglia |title=Mexico: No Coronavirus on MSC Meraviglia |work=The Maritime Executive |date=29 February 2020 |access-date=15 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320213241/https://www.maritime-executive.com/article/mexico-no-coronavirus-on-msc-meraviglia |archive-date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>
* {{ship||Norwegian Jewel}}: On 17 March 2020, the cruise ship was stranded in the middle of the Pacific Ocean, after being denied entry into [[Papeete]], [[French Polynesia]], and [[Lautoka]], [[Fiji]], due to fears of possible infection.<ref name=autogenerated1 /> On 19 March the 1,700 passengers were prevented from disembarking in [[Honolulu]], Hawaii.<ref name=honolulu /> On 23 March, the passengers were allowed to disembark in Honolulu because the ship was experiencing mechanical problems. Passengers were able to catch chartered flights to return to their home locations.  There were no confirmed cases of COVID-19 found aboard the ship.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.staradvertiser.com/2020/03/23/breaking-news/norwegian-jewel-cruise-ship-passengers-disembark-at-honolulu-harbor-bused-to-airport/ |title=Norwegian Jewel cruise ship passengers disembark at Honolulu Harbor, bused to airport |work=Honolulu Star Advertiser |last=Sinco Kelleher |first=Jennifer |agency=Associated Press |date=23 March 2020 |access-date=25 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324154109/https://www.staradvertiser.com/2020/03/23/breaking-news/norwegian-jewel-cruise-ship-passengers-disembark-at-honolulu-harbor-bused-to-airport/ |archive-date=24 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>  Approximately 1,000 crew members remained on the ship as of 27 March 2020.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://aashtojournal.org/2020/03/27/hawaii-dot-helps-get-2000-cruise-line-passengers-home/ |title=Hawaii DOT Helps Get 2,000 Cruise Line Passengers Home  |date=27 March 2020 |publisher=The American Association of State Highway and Transportation Officials |access-date=30 March 2020 }}</ref> On 10 April, 47 Filipino crew members arrived in [[Manila]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://manilastandard.net/mobile/article/321340|title=47 Pinoy seafarers of stranded Norwegian cruise ship arrive in Manila|accessdate=3 July 2020}}</ref><!-- although, at one point, there may have been people that suspected that there may have been cases of coronavirus on board, this ship should currently stay in the "no currently suspected cases" section as passengers were tested and both officials from the state of hawaii and the cruise line have mentioned that there were no suspected or confirmed cases on board.  of course, should there be a (justified) reason to suspect that cases have appeared on board since then, this ship should be moved to the "suspected cases" section. -->
* {{anchor|Pacific Princess}} {{ship||Pacific Princess}}: Though there have been no confirmed cases on board, the ship was rejected from docking at numerous destinations including [[Bali]], [[Singapore]], [[Phuket Province|Phuket, Thailand]], and [[Sri Lanka]]. The ship was as at 20 March 2020 en route to an uncertain future for [[Fremantle]], [[Australia]].<ref name=autogenerated1 /> Most passengers were allowed to disembark in Australia on 21 March; four were allowed to disembark in [[Honolulu]] on 13 April 2020.<ref name="pacific.hawaii">[https://www.hawaiinewsnow.com/2020/04/13/residents-allowed-disembark-cruise-ship-docked-honolulu-harbor/ 4 residents allowed to disembark from cruise ship docked at Honolulu Harbor] Hawaii News Now 13 April 2020</ref> The last remaining passengers disembarked when the ship returned to Los Angeles on 20 April.<ref>[https://nymag.com/intelligencer/2020/04/the-last-three-cruise-ships-at-sea-are-finally-going-home.html The Last Three Cruise Ships at Sea Are Finally Going Home] New York Magazine 20 April 2020</ref>
* {{anchor|Regal Princess}} {{ship||Regal Princess|2013|2}}:
** On 7 March, two crew members of ''Regal Princess'' were tested and the docking of the ship at [[Port Everglades]] in [[Fort Lauderdale]], [[Florida]], [[United States|U.S.]], was delayed for about a day while waiting for test results. The tests were negative, and the crew did not have respiratory complications, so the ship was allowed to dock.
** On 10 May 2020, a 39-year-old female Ukrainian crew member of ''Regal Princess'' died after going overboard from the ship while it was docked in [[Rotterdam]].<ref name="regal.law">[https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/05/articles/disease/crew-member-from-regal-princess-goes-overboard-during-final-repatriation-cruise/ Crew Member from Regal Princess Goes Overboard During Final Repatriation Cruise] Cruise Law News 10 May 2020</ref>  One source stated that she had committed suicide, and that she had been scheduled to be repatriated on a charter flight which was subsequently cancelled.<ref name="regal.crew">[http://crew-center.com/crew-member-goes-overboard-regal-princess Crew Member Goes Overboard from Regal Princess] CrewCenter 10 May 2020</ref> She was reportedly distraught and last seen crying aboard the ship.<ref name="regal.law" /><ref name="herald.royal.5" />
* {{ship||Royal Princess|2012|2}}: As a crew member from ''Grand Princess'' had transferred to ''Royal Princess'' fifteen days earlier, the CDC issued a "no-sail order" for ''Royal Princess'' on 8 March 2020, prompting Princess Cruises to cancel the ship's seven-day cruise to Mexico before it departed Los Angeles.<ref name="brochure" /><ref>{{cite web |title=Cruise out of Port of LA canceled after CDC issues 'no-sail order' over coronavirus concerns |url=https://abc7.com/health/cruise-out-of-port-of-la-canceled-after-cdc-issues-no-sail-order/5995426/ |website=ABC7 Los Angeles |language=en |date=8 March 2020 |access-date=8 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200309151545/https://abc7.com/health/cruise-out-of-port-of-la-canceled-after-cdc-issues-no-sail-order/5995426/ |archive-date=9 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last1=Munguia |first1=Hayley |title=Finally! Cruise passengers eagerly disembark the Carnival Panorama in Long Beach |url=https://www.presstelegram.com/2020/03/08/finally-cruise-passengers-eagerly-disembark-the-carnival-panorama-in-long-beach/ |website=Press Telegram |date=8 March 2020 |access-date=8 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200309014610/https://www.presstelegram.com/2020/03/08/finally-cruise-passengers-eagerly-disembark-the-carnival-panorama-in-long-beach/ |archive-date=9 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>
* {{anchor|Scarlet Lady}} {{ship||Scarlet Lady}}: On 22 May 2020, ''Cruise Law News'' reported that a male Filipino crew member of ''Scarlet Lady'' had been found dead in his cabin.<ref name="scarlet.law">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/05/articles/disease/crew-member-dies-on-virgin-voyages-lady-scarlet/|title=Crew Member Dies on Virgin Voyages' Scarlet Lady|date=22 May 2020|website=Cruise Law News}}</ref>  Colleagues believe he may have committed suicide, and the [[United States Coast Guard]] stated that the 32-year-old had died from "apparent self-harm".<ref name="scarlet.law" /><ref name="scarlet.herald">https://www.miamiherald.com/news/coronavirus/article242963031.html</ref>  The crew member had worked as a hotel utility employee.<ref name="scarlet.law" />  The ship had been located off the coast of [[Florida]] at the time, and sailed into [[PortMiami]] later that day, where police boarded the ship to conduct an investigation and the body was disembarked.<ref name="scarlet.law" /><ref name="scarlet.herald" />  ''Scarlet Lady'' is [[Virgin Voyages]]' inaugural ship, and Virgin Voyages had announced the previous day that its first sailing would be postponed to 16 October 2020.{{efn|The inaugural season had already been postponed once before.<ref name="scarlet.seatrade.1">{{cite web|url=https://www.seatrade-cruise.com/news/virgin-voyages-postpones-inaugural-season-until-july-15|title=Virgin Voyages postpones inaugural season until July 15|date=12 March 2020|website=seatrade-cruise.com}}</ref>}}<ref name="scarlet.virgin">{{cite web|url=https://www.virginvoyages.com/press/latest-releases/delivery-of-scarlet-lady|title=Virgin Voyages Welcomes Scarlet Lady|website=Virgin Voyages}}</ref><ref name="scarlet.seatrade.2">{{cite web|url=https://www.seatrade-cruise.com/news/virgin-voyages-cancels-sailings-through-oct-15-rolls-out-flexible-policy|title=Virgin Voyages cancels sailings through Oct. 15, rolls out flexible policy|date=21 May 2020|website=seatrade-cruise.com}}</ref>  A spokesperson for Virgin Voyages stated that the crew member was not waiting to be repatriated.<ref name="scarlet.herald" />
* {{anchor|Vasco da Gama}} {{ship||Vasco da Gama|ship|2}}:
** The cruise ship docked in [[Fremantle, Western Australia|Fremantle]] in late March 2020. Almost 100 New Zealand passengers were flown from [[Perth]] on 29 March and arrived in [[Auckland]] on 30 March. As of 31 March, about 200 West Australian passengers were to be ferried to [[Rottnest Island]], which had been converted to a quarantine zone. Another 600 Australians were to be taken to Perth hotels for 14 days of quarantine.<ref name="ABC-30-3-2020"/>
** On 19 May, a male Indonesian crew member of ''Vasco da Gama'' fell from deck 12 of the ship while it was docked at the [[Port of Tilbury]], London's main port, and landed on a cargo container that was placed on the dock next to the ship.<ref name="vasco.law">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/05/articles/disease/crew-member-seriously-injured-after-falling-from-vasco-da-gama/|title=Crew Member Seriously Injured After falling From Vasco da Gama|date=20 May 2020|website=Cruise Law News}}</ref>  One source reported that he died from the fall, while another reported that he was seriously injured but there was no confirmation that he had died, and a third reported that he was being treated at a hospital.<ref name="vasco.crew">{{cite web|url=https://crew-center.com/indonesian-crew-member-goes-overboard-cmv-cruise-ship|title=Indonesian Crew Member Goes Overboard From CMV Cruise Ship &#124; Crew Center|website=crew-center.com}}</ref><ref name="vasco.law" /><ref name="vasco.nub">{{cite web|url=https://thurrock.nub.news/n/crew-member-in-hospital-after-falling-from-cruise-ship-moored-up-at-port-of-tilbury|title=Crew member in hospital after falling from cruise ship moored up at Port of Tilbury|website=thurrock.nub.news}}</ref>  The crew member worked as a storekeeper in the ship's supply area.<ref name="vasco.crew" />  ''Vasco da Gama'' had been docked at Tilbury since 1 May, after having repatriated passengers to Australia.<ref name="vasco.law" />  Crew members have complained that they have not been paid and are frustrated with [[Cruise & Maritime Voyages]].{{efn|For example, one crew member complained that they have not been paid for work since April; that they have been locked up for two months, with neither alcohol nor cigarettes, only water and juice; and that Wi-Fi has only been available starting at midnight.<ref name="vasco.crew" />}}<ref name="vasco.crew" /><ref name="vasco.law" />

== Docking restrictions ==

''[[COVID-19 pandemic on cruise ships#World Dream|World Dream]]'' was turned away from Taiwan on 4 February. ''[[COVID-19 pandemic on cruise ships#Zaandam|Zaandam]]'' was turned away from [[Chile]] on 14 March, then was delayed passage through the [[Panama Canal]] and had to negotiate to disembark at [[Port Everglades|Port Everglades, United States]].

* Australia:
** Australia banned cruise ships arriving from foreign ports from 15 March 2020, and on 27 March directed all foreign-flagged ships to leave the country.<ref name=Grad0704>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: legal action could undo government order that cruise ships leave Australian waters |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/07/coronavirus-legal-action-could-undo-government-order-that-cruise-ships-leave-australian-waters |accessdate=10 April 2020 |newspaper=The Guardian |date=7 April 2020}}</ref> However the 2,700 passengers offloaded at [[Sydney]] on 19 March by the Australian-based ''[[COVID-19 pandemic on Ruby Princess|Ruby Princess]]'' had caused over 10% of all COVID-19 cases across that country by 10 April, and some ship operators challenged the Australian government's order in court.<ref name=Grad0704/>
** On 20 May 2020, the [[Minister for Health (Australia)|Minister for Health]] extended the ban on cruise ships arriving from foreign ports by another three months, to 17 September 2020.<ref name="docking.australia.abf">[https://newsroom.abf.gov.au/releases/cruise-ship-prohibition-extended CRUISE SHIP PROHIBITION EXTENDED] Australian Border Force 22 May 2020</ref>
* Canada:
** Canada blocked all ships carrying more than 500 people from docking in Canada from 13 March to 1 July 2020.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/british-columbia/coronavirus-update-bc-what-you-need-to-know-1.5495881|title=What you need to know about COVID-19 in B.C. on March 13, 2020|website=[[CBC News]]|access-date=14 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314030733/https://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/british-columbia/coronavirus-update-bc-what-you-need-to-know-1.5495881|archive-date=14 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>
** On 29 May 2020, the [[Minister of Transport (Canada)|Minister of Transport]] updated the restriction by announcing that "[c]ruise ships with overnight accommodations allowed to carry more than 100 persons" would not be allowed to operate in Canadian waters until 31 October 2020.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.canada.ca/en/transport-canada/news/2020/05/minister-garneau-announces-updated-measures-for-cruise-ships-and-passenger-vessels-in-canadian-waters-up-to-october-31-2020.html|title=Minister Garneau announces updated measures for cruise ships and passenger vessels in Canadian waters up to October 31, 2020|first=Transport|last=Canada|date=29 May 2020|website=gcnws|accessdate=3 July 2020}}</ref>
* New Zealand: New Zealand banned all cruise ships from entering New Zealand from 14 March 2020 to at least 30 June, with ships already in New Zealand waters allowed to complete their itinerary.<ref name="nz.ban">[https://covid19.govt.nz/individuals-and-households/travelling-and-moving-around/cruise-ships/ Cruise ships are currently banned from coming into New Zealand. You should avoid all non-essential travel including cruise ships.] Unite Against Covid-19 New Zealand Government</ref><ref name="nz.health">[https://www.health.govt.nz/news-media/media-releases/covid-19-update-ruby-princess-and-celebrity-solstice-cruises COVID-19 Update on Ruby Princess and Celebrity Solstice cruises] Ministry of New Zealand Health 20 March 2020</ref>
* Seychelles: The government of Seychelles put all authorizations for cruise ships on hold until at least 2022.<ref name="seychelles.authorizations">{{cite web|url=https://youtube.com/watch?v=_102IdE3c9I&t=196 |title=7 p.m News 08-05-2020 |publisher=YouTube |accessdate=2020-05-23}}</ref>
* Singapore: Singapore ceased port calls for all cruise ships on 13 March 2020.<ref>{{cite web|title=Covid-19: S'pore rolls out more measures including limiting, where possible, size of gatherings to 250 people; workplace distancing|url=https://www.straitstimes.com/singapore/health/covid-19-singapore-rolls-out-more-measures-including-limiting-where-possible-the|last1=Toh|first1=Ting Wei|last2=Khalik|first2=Salma|date=13 March 2020|website=The Straits Times|accessdate=9 April 2020}}</ref>
* United States: The [[United States Coast Guard]] declared that foreign-flagged vessels carrying more than 50 people should not dock in [[Florida]], [[Georgia (U.S. state)|Georgia]], [[South Carolina]], and [[Puerto Rico]] from 29 March, and instead should prepare to treat any sick passengers and crew on board and try to medically evacuate the very sick to their home countries.<ref>{{cite news |agency=Associated Press |title=Coast Guard: Cruise ships must stay at sea with sick onboard |first1=Freida |last1=Frisaro |first2=Adriana |last2=Gomez Licon |name-list-style=amp |date=1 April 2020 |url=https://news.yahoo.com/coast-guard-cruise-ships-must-122752320.html |work=Yahoo News |access-date=1 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200401125152/https://news.yahoo.com/coast-guard-cruise-ships-must-122752320.html |archive-date=1 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

== Government travel advisories ==

* Germany: The crisis management team of the German federal government said on 4 March 2020, following several actual and suspected outbreaks on cruise ships, "The Federal Foreign Office has included in its travel advice that there is an increased risk of quarantine on cruise ships."<ref name=berliner/>
* New Zealand: New Zealand advised against all nonessential travel, including on cruise ships.<ref name="nz.ban" />
* United Kingdom:
** On {{dts|2020.03.12|format=dmy}}, the [[Foreign and Commonwealth Office|Foreign & Commonwealth Office]] (FCO) advised British nationals that either had pre-existing health conditions or were at least 70 years old against travelling on cruise ships.<ref>https://web.archive.org/web/20200314220303/https://www.gov.uk/guidance/cruise-ship-travel</ref>
** On {{dts|2020.07.09|format=dmy}}, the FCO advised against travelling on cruise ships.<ref>https://web.archive.org/web/20200710103710/https://www.gov.uk/guidance/cruise-ship-travel</ref>
* United States: The [[Centers for Disease Control and Prevention]] remarks that "[o]utbreaks of COVID-19 on cruise ships pose a risk for rapid spread of disease beyond the voyage" and that "[a]ggressive efforts are required to contain spread".<ref name="advisory.cdc">{{cite web|url=https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/travelers/cruise-ship/what-cdc-is-doing.html |title=CDC's role in helping cruise ship travelers during the COVID-19 pandemic &#124; CDC |publisher=Cdc.gov |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref>  They recommend that "cruise ship travelers with no symptoms or mild symptoms disembark as quickly and safely as possible at US ports of entry", disallowing the usage of "[c]ommercial flights and public transportation", and requiring the usage of "chartered or private transportation" instead.<ref name="advisory.cdc" /> A US Coast Guard report on 4 April 2020 stated that "there are 114 cruise ships, carrying 93,000 crew members, either in or near U.S. ports and waters. ... Another 41 cruise ships, with 41,000 crew members, are underway and close to the U.S".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.ctvnews.ca/health/coronavirus/another-cruise-ship-with-virus-victims-docking-in-florida-1.4882574 |title=Another cruise ship with virus victims docking in Florida |publisher=CTV News, The Associated Press |date=4 April 2020 |access-date=4 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200405021519/https://www.ctvnews.ca/health/coronavirus/another-cruise-ship-with-virus-victims-docking-in-florida-1.4882574 |archive-date=5 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

== International rules proposal ==

In response to the delayed action over the coronavirus outbreak [[#Diamond Princess|aboard ''Diamond Princess'']] and the confusion over the outbreak [[#Costa Atlantica|aboard ''Costa Atlantica'']], Japan has budgeted about 60 million [[Japanese yen|JPY]] for research into developing a set of international rules to govern outbreaks of infectious diseases aboard cruise ships.<ref name="japan.yomiuri">{{cite web|url=https://the-japan-news.com/news/article/0006525599 |title=Japan eyes international rules for cruise ship outbreaks |publisher=the-japan-news.com |date=24 March 2020 |accessdate=2020-05-23}}</ref>  Since countries would be dissuaded from allowing ships with outbreaks on board from docking if they were entirely responsible for a ship docking in their ports, and [[jurisdiction]] is unclear when a ship docks in a country other than its [[flag state]],{{efn|This may be further complicated when the flag state refuses to take any appropriate action, or when a ship is merely flying a [[flag of convenience]], with the owners of the ship belonging to a country other than the flag state.<ref name="japan.yomiuri" />}} the Japanese government believed that a set of rules should be drafted to address such issues.<ref name="japan.yomiuri" />  The government hoped to have the rules adopted by other countries as well as international bodies such as the [[International Maritime Organization]] and the [[World Health Organization]].<ref name="japan.yomiuri" />

== Cruise line suspensions ==

On 11 March 2020, [[Viking Cruises]] suspended operations for its 79-vessel fleet until the end of April, cancelling all ocean and river cruises, after it was revealed that a passenger on a cruise in Cambodia had been exposed to the virus while in transit via plane, placing at least 28 other passengers in quarantine.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.vikingrivercruises.com.au/my-trip/current-sailings/index.html|title=My Trip – Updates on Current Sailings|website=vikingrivercruises.com.au|access-date=12 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200312181910/https://www.vikingrivercruises.com.au/my-trip/current-sailings/index.html|archive-date=12 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.businessinsider.com/viking-cruises-coronavirus-suspends-operations-industry-struggles-2020-3 |title=Viking Cruises suspended operations worldwide due to the coronavirus, as infections ravage the cruise industry |first=Bill |last=Bostock |website=Business Insider |date=12 March 2020 |access-date=12 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200312174617/https://www.businessinsider.com/viking-cruises-coronavirus-suspends-operations-industry-struggles-2020-3 |archive-date=12 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

Similarly, on 12 March, [[Princess Cruises]], owner of virus-stricken ships ''Diamond Princess'' and {{ship||Grand Princess}}, suspended operations for all future cruises on its 18-ship fleet for 60 days.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.princess.com/news/notices_and_advisories/notices/global-ship-operations-pause.html|title=Princess Cruises: Voluntary 60 Day Pause of Global Ship Operations – Notices & Advisories|publisher=Princess Cruises|date=12 March 2020|website=princess.com|access-date=12 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200312190604/https://www.princess.com/news/notices_and_advisories/notices/global-ship-operations-pause.html|archive-date=12 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/12/coronavirus-viking-cruises-suspends-cruise-operations-until-may-1/5030006002/ |title=Princess Cruises suspends operations for 60 days; Viking Cruises cancels all cruises due to coronavirus |first1=Hannah |last1=Yasharoff |first2=Morgan |last2=Hines |last3=Tate |first3=Curtis |name-list-style=amp |website=[[USA Today]] |date=12 March 2020 |access-date=12 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200312203258/https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/12/coronavirus-viking-cruises-suspends-cruise-operations-until-may-1/5030006002/ |archive-date=12 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

All cruise lines suspended departures from the United States on 14 March.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://cruising.org:443/news-and-research/press-room/2020/march/clia-covid-19-toolkit|title=CLIA Announces Voluntary Suspension in U.S. Cruise Operations|website=Cruise Line Industry Association}}</ref>

On {{dts|2020.06.30|format=dmy}}, [[Celestyal Cruises]] announced that it was voluntarily extending its suspension of all cruise operations until {{dts|2021.03.06|format=dmy}}.<ref>https://www.celestyalcruises.com/en/celestyal-cruises-voluntarily-extends-suspension-of-cruise-operations-until-2021-due-to-ongoing</ref><ref>https://www.maritime-executive.com/article/celestyal-announces-suspension-of-cruising-through-end-of-2020</ref>

==Crew strandings and repatriations==

After disembarking passengers, many cruise ships remained docked or at sea near ports with crew members still aboard, in some cases unpaid though with free room and board.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/2020/05/03/849732492/many-crews-remain-aboard-cruise-ships-after-passengers-evacuated|title=Many Crews Remain Aboard Cruise Ships After Passengers Evacuated|website=NPR.org}}</ref> Crew members are generally citizens of many different countries, aside from those where the ship is registered, based, or temporarily stopped. Especially with pandemic-related travel restrictions and concerns about onboard outbreaks, crew members could not simply disembark and fly home. After some negotiations, most cruise companies made special arrangements to allow crew members to take charter flights to their home countries. In some cases, the ships themselves were used to transport crew members to home countries directly.<ref name="herald_unhappy">{{cite web | last1=Charles | first1=Jacqueline | last2=Dolven | first2=Taylor | title=Cruise lines finally repatriating workers stranded by COVID-19. Not everyone is happy | website=miamiherald | date=2020-05-12 | url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/business/tourism-cruises/article242673546.html | access-date=2020-05-23}}</ref> According to the ''[[Miami Herald]]'', [[Royal Caribbean International|Royal Caribbean]] has been slower than other companies to make these arrangements; in the meantime two crew members have died after jumping overboard, and some crew on ''Navigator of the Seas'' have gone on hunger strike demanding to be released.<ref name="herald_unhappy" /> The government of [[Grenada]] complained that cruise companies that promised to pay for on-shore quarantines failed to do so, and some were concerned about crew members being released into Haiti from Royal Caribbean ships without testing or on-shore quarantine.<ref name="herald_unhappy" />

=== Incidents ===

* {{ship||Majesty of the Seas}}: On 15 May 2020, about 400 crew members protested because their scheduled repatriation date had been rescheduled for a fifth time.{{efn|The previous five repatriation dates were 26 April, 28 April, 4 May, 14 May, and 18 May 2020.<ref name="majesty.incident.crew" />}}<ref name="majesty.incident.crew">{{cite web|url=http://crew-center.com/royal-caribbean-crew-stage-protest-aboard-majesty-seas|title=Royal Caribbean Crew Stage Protest Aboard Majesty of the Seas &#124; Crew Center|website=crew-center.com}}</ref>  Crew members have been stuck aboard the ship for at least 60 days.<ref name="majesty.incident.crew" /><ref name="majesty.incident.law">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/05/articles/disease/63-days-stuck-at-sea-protest-erupts-on-royal-caribbeans-majesty-of-the-seas/|title=63 Days Stuck at Sea: Protest Erupts on Royal Caribbean's Majesty of the Seas|date=16 May 2020|website=Cruise Law News}}</ref>  One sign erected by the protesters read "How many more suicides do you need?!",{{efn|Sign was in all capital letters.<ref name="majesty.incident.law" />|name="allcaps"}} referring to the deaths of a Polish engineer aboard {{ship||Jewel of the Seas}} and a Chinese assistant waiter aboard {{ship||Mariner of the Seas}}.<ref name="majesty.incident.law" />  Another read "Do you sleep well M. Bailey?!",<!-- name was misspelt on sign -->{{efn|name="allcaps"}} referring to [[Royal Caribbean International]] CEO Michael Bayley, who received around US$25,000,000 in compensation over the past four years, while a spokesperson for the [[Centers for Disease Control and Prevention|CDC]] had stated that cruise line officials had complained that arranging private transportation for the crew was "too expensive".<ref name="majesty.incident.law" /><ref name="herald.royal.1" /><!-- note: cruise law news stated that the miami herald reported that michael bayley said it was "too expensive", although one miami herald article covering the issue only reported that a spokesperson for the cdc said cruise line officials were complaining about it, without explicitly stating that ceo bayley said so -->

== Hazard controls ==
{{Further|Workplace hazard controls for COVID-19}}
According to the U.S. [[Centers for Disease Control and Prevention]], proper [[Hierarchy of hazard controls|hazard controls]] for cruise ships and other commercial vessels include postponing travel when sick, and self-isolating and informing the onboard medical center immediately if one develops a fever or other symptoms while on board.  Ideally, medical follow-up should occur in the isolated person's cabin.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cdc.gov/quarantine/maritime/recommendations-for-ships.html|title=Interim Guidance for Ships on Managing Suspected Coronavirus Disease 2019|date=2020-02-18|website=U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention|access-date=2020-03-21|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200301220052/https://www.cdc.gov/quarantine/maritime/recommendations-for-ships.html|archive-date=1 March 2020|url-status=live}} {{PD-inline}}</ref>

A new regulation issued by the CDC on 6 April 2020 stated that passengers on cruise ships would not be able to travel home on commercial flights. They were to travel only by "charter flights and private transportation".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://edition.cnn.com/world/live-news/coronavirus-pandemic-04-06-20/index.html |title=South Florida could be the most impacted by new restrictions on cruise travelers |date=6 April 2020 |publisher=CNN |access-date=6 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406022613/https://edition.cnn.com/world/live-news/coronavirus-pandemic-04-06-20/index.html |archive-date=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

== Resuming cruise operations ==
<!-- sorted by date cruise operations were resumed -->

* <!-- resumed 2020.06.16 --> Norwegian cruise line [[Hurtigruten AS]] was the first ocean cruise line in the world to resume cruise operations, with {{MS|Otto Sverdrup||2}} sailing from [[Bergen]] to [[Kirkenes]] on {{dts|2020.06.16|format=dmy}}.{{r|sverdrup.mapper}}{{r|sverdrup.critic}}  The first large outbreak of coronavirus on a cruise ship after the resumption of cruise operations was also aboard a Hurtigruten ship, with 36 people that were aboard Hurtigruten's {{MS|Roald Amundsen||2}} [[#Roald Amundsen|testing positive after docking]] at Tromsø {{as of|2020|08|01|lc=y}}.{{r|amundsen.nordlys.02}}
* <!-- resumed 2020.07.18 --> [[Compagnie du Ponant]] resumed cruise operations on {{dts|2020.07.18|format=dmy}} with a [[French Polynesia]]n cruise for the local market.{{r|gauguin.seatrade}}<ref name="ponant.seatrade">https://www.seatrade-cruise.com/news/paul-gauguin-restart-july-french-polynesia-opens-all-travelers</ref>  Its first cruise for international travellers set sail on {{dts|2020.07.30|format=dm}}, and was abruptly halted on {{dts|2020.08.01|format=dm}} when one of the passengers aboard ''[[Paul Gauguin (ship)|Paul Gauguin]]'' [[#Paul Gauguin|tested positive for the virus]].{{r|gauguin.seatrade}}
* <!-- resumed 2020.07.24 --> [[TUI Cruises]] resumed cruise operations with the departure of {{ill|Mein Schiff 2 (2019)|lt=''Mein Schiff 2''|de|Mein Schiff 2 (Schiff, 2019)}} from [[Hamburg]] on {{dts|2020.07.24|format=dmy}} for a three-day roundtrip voyage in the [[North Sea]], making no intermediate stops.<ref name="schiff2.dw">https://www.dw.com/en/first-cruise-ship-sets-sail-from-german-harbor-since-coronavirus-lockdown/a-54315272</ref>  About 1200 passengers were aboard, although TUI Cruises had set a quota of 1740, and the ship's capacity was around 2900.{{r|schiff2.dw}}  Passengers were required to fill out a health questionnaire prior to boarding, and were not allowed to serve themselves from the buffet table.{{r|schiff2.dw}}  Another [[#Mein Schiff 1|cruise aboard ''Mein Schiff 1'' was cancelled]], ostensibly because a crew could not be assembled in time due to coronavirus travel restrictions.{{r|schiff1.law}}{{r|schiff1.crew}}  TUI Cruises later admitted that it was because five crew members of ''Mein Schiff 1'' had tested positive.{{r|schiff1.kfat}}
*A cruise ship sailed in November 2020 from and to Singapore on a three-day roundtrip voyage in the Malacca Strait, making no intermediate stops.<ref>{{cite web |title=Cruise Industry Reinvents Itself With Trips to Nowhere |url=https://www.wsj.com/video/cruise-industry-reinvents-itself-with-trips-to-nowhere/EAAD5F4F-8CE7-4F98-8FF2-01770E9E55E3.html?mod=trending_now_video_2 |publisher=WSJ |date=20 November 2020}}</ref> On 9 December it was reported that an 83 year old had been diagnosed with covid-19, which led to that "cruise to nowhere" being cut short.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Pitrelli|first=Monica Buchanan|date=2020-12-09|title=Even 'cruises to nowhere' can't escape the coronavirus|url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/12/09/a-covid-19-infection-is-found-on-a-singapore-cruise-to-nowhere.html|access-date=2020-12-10|website=CNBC|language=en}}</ref> After retesting the original sample, and taking a second sample, the case appeared to be a false positive.<ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-12-08|title=Royal Caribbean Guests Are in Limbo After False Covid Diagnosis|language=en|work=Bloomberg.com|url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-12-08/cruise-to-nowhere-returns-to-singapore-on-possible-covid-19-risk|access-date=2020-12-10}}</ref>

==Financial fallout==
{{See also|Economic impact of the COVID-19 pandemic|Financial market impact of the COVID-19 pandemic}}
Cruise line stock fell sharply on 27 March 2020 when the US$2 trillion relief package passed by the U.S. Congress and signed by [[Donald Trump|President Trump]] excluded companies that are not "organized" under United States law. [[Carnival Corporation & plc]] is registered in Panama, England and Wales; [[Royal Caribbean International]] is chartered in Liberia, and [[Norwegian Cruise Line Holdings]] is domiciled in Bermuda. Senator [[Sheldon Whitehouse]], (D-RI), tweeted: "The giant cruise companies incorporate overseas to dodge US taxes, flag vessels overseas to avoid US taxes and laws, and pollute without offset. Why should we bail them out?" Senator [[Josh Hawley]] (R-MO) tweeted that cruise lines should register and pay taxes in the United States if they expect a financial bailout. U.S-based employees and American-owned passenger ships will still be eligible for financial assistance.<ref>{{cite web |website=Associated Press |title=Cruise stocks sink after missing out on economic-relief bill |first1=David |last1=Koening |first2=Kevin |last2=Freking |name-list-style=amp |date=27 March 2020 |url=https://apnews.com/819d004059e6b165d9509f2d346a7d41 |access-date=30 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200329192618/https://apnews.com/819d004059e6b165d9509f2d346a7d41 |archive-date=29 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> [[Carnival Cruise Line]] stock fell 75% between 1 January and 31 March 2020 and dividend payments to shareholders were suspended. On 13 March the company drew down its $3 billion revolving credit line and [[Moody's Investors Service|Moody's]] and [[S&P Global]] downgraded Carnival's debt rating. On 31 March Carnival announced plans to issue $1.25 billion in stock and $4.75 billion in notes due in 2023. The [[Cruise Lines International Association]], a cruise line [[trade association]], claims that the cruise industry supports 400,000 jobs in the United States.<ref>[https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/31/cruise-ship-company-carnival-to-raise-6-billion-in-stock-and-debt-shares-jump.html?recirc=taboolainternal Beleaguered cruise ship company Carnival to raise $6 billion in stock and debt, shares jump] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200401170947/https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/31/cruise-ship-company-carnival-to-raise-6-billion-in-stock-and-debt-shares-jump.html?recirc=taboolainternal |date=1 April 2020 }} by William Feuer, [[CNBC]], 31 Mar 2020</ref>

A September 24, 2020 report by U.S. Federal Maritime Commissioner [[Louis E. Sola]] said Florida had lost $3.2 billion in economic activity and 49,500 local jobs that pay $2.3 billion in wages, as a result of the suspension of cruising in response to the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cruisehive.com/floridas-economy-needs-cruise-lines-to-start-operations/42152 |title=Florida’s Economy Needs Cruise Lines To Start Operations|date=2020-09-27|website=cruisehive.com|language=en-US|access-date=2020-10-10}}</ref>

== Average age of cruise passengers ==

A report from [[Cruise Lines International Association]] from 2019 states the [[Arithmetic mean|average]] age of cruise passengers is 46.9 years, while the largest age bracket is 60–69 years (19%) followed by 50–59 years (18%).<ref>Darcy Alexander: ''[https://www.cruise1st.co.uk/blog/cruise-holidays/how-old-is-the-average-cruise-passenger/ How Old is the Average Cruise Passenger?] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403212942/https://www.cruise1st.co.uk/blog/cruise-holidays/how-old-is-the-average-cruise-passenger/ |date=3 April 2020 }}'', Cruise 1st, 23 August 2019</ref> Research from 2001 studying the epidemiology of passenger mortalities on two cruise ships, indicated a median age of 65 years of cruise participants. It also stated, that between April 1995 to April 2001 "there was an average of one death every six months per ship", with an average of 800 passengers on each ship.<ref>Eilif Dahl: ''[https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11817837 Passenger mortalities aboard cruise ships]'', University of Oslo, Department of Surgery, The [[Oslo University Hospital, Rikshospitalet|National Hospital (Rikshospitalet)]], Norway, published in [[International Maritime Health Association|International Maritime Health]], 2001</ref>

{{short description|Ongoing COVID-19 viral pandemic on cruise ships}}
{{Use dmy dates|date=March 2020}}
{{EngvarB|date=February 2020}}
{{COVID-19 pandemic sidebar|expanded=locations}}

<!-- please do not add excessive references to sars-cov-2 or covid-19 to the lead, as this page is focused on the pandemic on cruise ships, and not the virus or the disease itself.  in addition, the sidebar also has links for the virus and the disease in bold if the user is interested. -->The [[COVID-19 pandemic]] spread to a number of [[cruise ship]]s, with the nature of such ships—including crowded semi-enclosed areas, increased exposure to new environments, and limited medical resources—contributing to the heightened risk and rapid spread of the disease.<ref>{{cite web|first1=Kara |last1=Tardivel |first2=Stefanie B. |last2=White |first3=Krista Kornylo |last3=Duong |url=https://wwwnc.cdc.gov/travel/yellowbook/2020/travel-by-air-land-sea/cruise-ship-travel |title=Cruise Ship Travel – Chapter 8 – 2020 Yellow Book &#124; Travelers' Health &#124; CDC |publisher=C.cdc.gov |date=2019-06-24 |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref>

The British-registered {{ship||Diamond Princess|ship|2}} was the first cruise ship to have a major outbreak on board, with the ship [[quarantine]]d at [[Port of Yokohama|Yokohama]] from 4 February 2020 for approximately one month.  Over 700 people [[COVID-19 pandemic on Diamond Princess|became infected]], and 14 people died. At the time, the ship accounted for over half the reported cases of [[Severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2|SARS-CoV-2]] outside of mainland [[China]].<ref name="theguardian1">{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/live/2020/feb/20/coronavirus-live-updates-diamond-princess-cruise-ship-japan-deaths-latest-news-china-infections |title=Cruise ship accounts for more than half of virus cases outside China – as it happened |newspaper=The Guardian |date=20 February 2020 |accessdate=5 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304102207/https://www.theguardian.com/world/live/2020/feb/20/coronavirus-live-updates-diamond-princess-cruise-ship-japan-deaths-latest-news-china-infections |archive-date=4 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

Governments and ports responded by [[#Docking restrictions|preventing]] many cruise ships from docking and [[#Government travel advisories|advising]] people to avoid travelling on cruise ships.  Similarly, [[#Cruise line suspensions|many cruise lines suspended]] their operations to mitigate the spread of the pandemic.

{{As of|2020|05|02}}, over 40 cruise ships have had [[#Summary of confirmed cases on board|confirmed positive cases]] of coronavirus on board.  The last cruise ship with passengers aboard during the first wave of the pandemic, {{ship|MV|Artania||2}}, docked at its home port with its last eight passengers on 8 June 2020.{{efn|''Arcadia'' had previously docked in Australia, but was required by the Australian government to undock.}}<ref name="final.cnn" /><ref name="guardian.status">{{cite web|first1=Erin |last1=McCormick |first2=Patrick |last2=Greenfield |first3=Uki |last3=Goñi |url=https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2020/apr/09/revealed-6000-passengers-on-cruise-ships-at-sea-despite-coronavirus-crisis |title=Revealed: 6,000 passengers on cruise ships despite coronavirus crisis &#124; World news |newspaper=The Guardian |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref><ref name="newsweek.status">{{cite web|last=Impelli |first=Matthew |url=https://www.newsweek.com/eight-cruise-ships-still-carrying-passengers-sea-coronavirus-cases-grow-around-world-1496034 |title=Eight Cruise Ships Still Carrying Passengers At Sea As Coronavirus Cases Grow Around The World |work=Newsweek |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref><ref name="artania.cbs" /><ref name="deliziosa.gazzettino" /><ref name="artania.phoenix" /><ref name="artania.tricks">{{Cite web|url=https://www.cruisetricks.de/artania-die-letzten-acht-kreuzfahrtschiff-passagiere-sind-zurueck-in-der-heimat/|title=Artania: Die letzten acht Kreuzfahrtschiff-Passagiere sind zurück in der Heimat|date=8 June 2020|website=Cruisetricks.de Kreuzfahrt-Ratgeber|accessdate=3 July 2020}}</ref><ref name="artania.sukf.2">{{Cite web|url=https://www.schiffe-und-kreuzfahrten.de/news/morten-hansen-bringt-die-letzten-8-kreuzfahrtgaeste-nach-hause-ms-artania-in-bremerhaven/205220/|title=Morten Hansen bringt die letzten 8 Kreuzfahrtgäste nach Hause - MS Artania in Bremerhaven|date=8 June 2020|accessdate=3 July 2020}}</ref>  In addition, over 40,000 crew members remained on cruise ships, some in isolation, as of mid-June 2020.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.foxnews.com/travel/at-least-42000-cruise-ship-workers-still-at-sea |title=At least 42,000 cruise ship workers are still trapped at sea: report |date=15 June 2020 |publisher=Fox News|access-date=15 June 2020}}</ref> Many are unable to be [[repatriation|repatriated]] because cruise lines refuse to cover the cost of doing so,<ref name="crew.guardian">{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2020/apr/30/no-end-in-sight-100000-crew-on-cruise-ships-stranded-at-sea-coronavirus |title=Revealed: 100,000 crew never made it off cruise ships amid coronavirus crisis|first1=Erin|last1=McCormick |first2=Patrick|last2=Greenfield |date=30 April 2020|via=www.theguardian.com |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200507114822/https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2020/apr/30/no-end-in-sight-100000-crew-on-cruise-ships-stranded-at-sea-coronavirus |url-status=live |archive-date=2020-05-07}}</ref><ref name="crew.law">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/04/articles/disease/100000-crew-members-stranded-on-cruise-ships-as-cruise-lines-refuse-to-agree-to-pay-for-repatriation-expenses/ |title=100,000 Crew Members Stranded on Cruise Ships as Cruise Lines Refuse to Agree to Pay for Repatriation Expenses|date=30 April 2020|website=Cruise Law News |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200503011243/https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/04/articles/disease/100000-crew-members-stranded-on-cruise-ships-as-cruise-lines-refuse-to-agree-to-pay-for-repatriation-expenses/ |url-status=live |archive-date=2020-05-03}}</ref> and because countries have different and changing rules. The condition is stressful to many employees.<!--some die from non-covid--><ref name=crewstress>{{cite web |title=Nightmare at Sea Ends In Death for Some Cruise Ship Workers |url=https://finance.yahoo.com/news/nightmare-sea-ends-death-cruise-095851490.html |website=finance.yahoo.com |publisher=Bloomberg |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200512181750/https://finance.yahoo.com/news/nightmare-sea-ends-death-cruise-095851490.html |archive-date=2020-05-12 |date=2020-05-12 |url-status=live}}</ref> Multiple suicides have been reported.<ref>{{cite web|title='I Really Need to Go Home': The Cruise Ship Employees Still Stuck at Sea|url=https://www.vice.com/en_us/article/g5pb54/i-really-need-to-go-home-the-cruise-ship-employees-still-stuck-at-sea|last=Yingst|first=Alexandra|date=2020-05-20|website=Vice|language=en|access-date=2020-05-21}}</ref>
