investigation |date=9 April 2020 |publisher=ABC|access-date=9 April 2020 }}</ref>

=== ''MSC Bellissima'' === <!-- 2020.03.21: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->

On 21 March 2020, officials from the [[States and union territories of India|Indian state]] of [[Telangana]] reported that a 33-year-old crew member of {{ship||MSC Bellissima||2}} had tested positive for the virus.<ref name="bellissima.telangana">[https://telanganatoday.com/two-more-persons-test-positive-for-covid-19-in-telangana Two more persons test positive for COVID-19 in Telangana] Telangana Today 27 April 2020</ref>  The crew member was also reported to have been to Dubai, and was stable at the time of the report.<ref name="bellissima.telangana" />

On 24 March 2020, it was reported that three [[Azores|Azoreans]] who were former passengers of ''MSC Bellissima'' during its cruise to Dubai from 7 March 2020 to 14 March had tested positive.{{efn|Two cases were from [[São Miguel Island]], a 31-year-old man and a 22-year-old woman, while one case from [[São Jorge Island]] had been diagnosed previously, but had been in contact with a newly-diagnosed case from [[Terceira Island]].<ref name="bellissima.oriental" />}}<ref name="bellissima.oriental">[https://www.acorianooriental.pt/noticia/acorianos-que-participaram-no-cruzeiro-devem-contactar-a-linha-saude-acores-308613 Açorianos que participaram no cruzeiro devem contactar a Linha Saúde Açores] Açoriano Oriental 24 March 2020</ref>

On 2 April 2020, a 22-year-old crew member of ''MSC Bellissima'', who had quarantined himself at home in [[Trappeto]], [[Sicily]], after returning from Dubai, announced that he had tested positive that day.<ref name="bellissima.sicilia">[https://www.direttasicilia.it/2020/04/02/trappeto-positivo-un-ragazzo-di-22-anni-che-lavorava-sulle-navi-msc/ Trappeto, positivo un ragazzo di 22 anni che lavorava sulle navi MSC] Diretta Sicillia 2 April 2020</ref>

On 10 April 2020, a dancer from [[Klagenfurt]], [[Austria]], who performed in [[Cirque du Soleil]] shows aboard ''MSC Bellissima'', tested positive for the virus while she was still on board the ship.<ref name="bellissima.orf">{{cite web|url=https://kaernten.orf.at/stories/3047045/|title=Kärntnerin sitzt seit 50 Tagen auf Schiff fest|first=kaernten ORF at|last=red|date=4 May 2020|website=kaernten.ORF.at}}</ref><ref name="bellissima.sukf">{{cite web|url=https://www.schiffe-und-kreuzfahrten.de/news/msc-kreuzfahrten-crew-nach-hause-geschickt-cirque-du-soleil-artistin-in-isolation-mit-positivem-befund/203599/|title=MSC Kreuzfahrten: Crew nach Hause geschickt - Cirque Du Soleil Artistin in Isolation mit positivem Befund|first=Uta|last=Waldhauser|date=5 May 2020}}</ref>  The crew member was tested a day before she was scheduled to leave for home, and the result came as a surprise as she had been asymptomatic.<ref name="bellissima.sukf" />  As of 4 May 2020, she has been stuck aboard ''MSC Bellissima'' for 50 days.<ref name="bellissima.orf" />

=== {{anchor|Ovation of the Seas}} ''Ovation of the Seas''{{efn|Included under ships with confirmed cases on board because it was reported that authorities unusually did not carry out any health checks or tests upon disembarkation.<ref name="ovation.abc" />|name="include.ovation"}} === <!-- 2020.03.21: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:Ovation of the Seas, Fremantle, 2016 (01).jpg|thumb|''Ovation of the Seas'' in 2016]]

In March 2020 thousands of passengers were ordered to self-isolate after disembarking from {{ship||Ovation of the Seas||2}} in [[Sydney]], Australia on 18 March due to [[COVID-19]] fears.<ref name="ovation.abc">{{cite web |url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-23/cruise-passengers-not-tested-for-coronavirus-before-disembarking/12081426 |title=Thousands of cruise ship passengers told to self-isolate due to coronavirus days after disembarking |last1=Farrell |first1=Paul |last2=McDonald |first2=Alex |name-list-style=amp |work=[[Australian Broadcasting Company|ABC]] |date=23 March 2020 |access-date=26 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200325010855/https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-23/cruise-passengers-not-tested-for-coronavirus-before-disembarking/12081426 |archive-date=25 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> [[Ministry of Health (New South Wales)|NSW Health]] reported the first positive case associated with ''Ovation of the Seas'' on 21 March 2020.<ref name="2020.03.21.nsw.health">{{cite web|url=https://www.health.nsw.gov.au/news/Pages/20200321_00.aspx |title=COVID-19 (Coronavirus) statistics – News |publisher=Health.nsw.gov.au |date=2020-03-21 |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref> 79 passengers subsequently tested positively for the virus. As of 1 April, the ship was located off the coast of [[New South Wales]]. The [[International Transport Workers' Federation]] had called on the Australian government to allow the crew members to be disembarked so that could be flown to their countries of residence.<ref name="guardian2020-04-01"/>

On 2 April, a 75-year-old man died in [[Wollongong Hospital]].<ref name="auto3"/> The ship departed Australia on 4 April 2020 with its crew.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/05/criminal-investigation-launched-ruby-princess-cruise-ship-coronavirus-disaster |title=Criminal investigation launched into Ruby Princess cruise ship coronavirus disaster |date=5 April 2020 |newspaper=The Guardian |access-date=5 April 2020 |quote=At least 11 passengers from ship have now died, more than 30% of Australia's total Covid-19 deaths |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200405083311/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/05/criminal-investigation-launched-ruby-princess-cruise-ship-coronavirus-disaster |archive-date=5 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

=== {{anchor|Voyager of the Seas}} ''Voyager of the Seas''{{efn|Included under ships with confirmed cases on board because, being owned by Royal Caribbean which also owned ''Ovation of the Seas'' and having disembarkation held on the same day as ''Ovation of the Seas'', it is likely that authorities also unusually did not carry out any health checks or tests upon disembarkation, as was reported regarding the disembarkation of ''Ovation of the Seas''.<ref name="ovation.abc" />|name="include.voyager"}} === <!-- 2020.03.21: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
Passengers disembarked from {{ship||Voyager of the Seas||2}} in [[Sydney]], Australia on 18 March.<ref name="ferrell1">{{cite web |url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-23/cruise-passengers-not-tested-for-coronavirus-before-disembarking/12081426 |title=Thousands of cruise ship passengers told to self-isolate due to coronavirus days after disembarking |last1=Ferrell |first1=Paul |last2=McDonald |first2=Alex |name-list-style=amp |work=[[Australian Broadcasting Corporation|ABC]].net |date=23 March 2020 |access-date=26 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200325010855/https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-23/cruise-passengers-not-tested-for-coronavirus-before-disembarking/12081426 |archive-date=25 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>  [[Ministry of Health (New South Wales)|NSW Health]] reported the first positive cases associated with ''Voyager of the Seas'' on 21 March 2020.<ref name="2020.03.21.nsw.health"/>

A man from [[Toowoomba]], Queensland, was infected on the ship and was sent into intensive care unit of a Toowoomba hospital after disembarking but died.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-25/queensland-man-dies-from-coronavirus-covid-19/12090804 |title=Coronavirus claims life of Toowoomba man infected on cruise ship who was allowed to travel home |work=ABC.net |date=25 March 2020 |access-date=26 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200325205344/https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-25/queensland-man-dies-from-coronavirus-covid-19/12090804 |archive-date=25 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 2 April 34 passengers and 5 crew members had tested positively for the virus in New South Wales alone.<ref name="nswhealth-2-4-2020">{{cite web|url=https://www.health.nsw.gov.au/news/Pages/20200402_00.aspx|title=COVID-19 (Coronavirus) statistics – News|date=2020-04-02|website=NSW Health|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404032526/https://www.health.nsw.gov.au/news/Pages/20200402_00.aspx|archive-date=4 April 2020|accessdate=2020-04-02}}</ref>

The ship departed Australia on 4 April 2020 with its crew.<ref name="theguardian2">{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/05/criminal-investigation-launched-ruby-princess-cruise-ship-coronavirus-disaster |title=Criminal investigation launched into Ruby Princess cruise ship coronavirus disaster |date=5 April 2020 |newspaper=The Guardian |access-date=5 April 2020 |quote=At least 11 passengers from ship have now died, more than 30% of Australia’s total Covid-19 deaths |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200405083311/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/05/criminal-investigation-launched-ruby-princess-cruise-ship-coronavirus-disaster |archive-date=5 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 23 April, a 79-year-old Kāpiti man named Bob James died from the disease while his wife has been infected and sick.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12326805|title=Covid 19 coronavirus on cruise ship Voyager of the Seas: Kāpiti man Bob James dies, wife sick|first=Melissa Nightingale NZ Herald reporter based in Wellington|last=melissa.nightingale@nzherald.co.nz @mel_nightingale|date=22 April 2020|via=www.nzherald.co.nz}}</ref>

=== ''Costa Victoria'' === <!-- 2020.03.24: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
{{ship||Costa Victoria}} left [[Dubai]] on 7 March 2020. A female Argentine national was tested positive and disembarked in [[Crete]]. 726 passengers were quarantined and managed to leave only after the ship docked in [[Civitavecchia]], near Rome, Italy, on 25 March.<ref name="Victoria_thelocal">{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: Fears on cruise ship docked at Italian port after case confirmed |url=https://www.thelocal.it/20200325/coronavirus-fears-on-cruise-ship-docked-in-rome-after-case-confirmed |accessdate=27 March 2020 |work=The Local Italy |agency=AFP |date=25 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327192655/https://www.thelocal.it/20200325/coronavirus-fears-on-cruise-ship-docked-in-rome-after-case-confirmed |archive-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Le Messurier |first1=Danielle |title=West Live: Perth couple stranded on Costa Victoria cruise ship where COVID-19 case confirmed |url=https://thewest.com.au/news/coronavirus/west-live-perth-couple-stranded-on-costa-victoria-cruise-ship-where-covid-19-case-confirmed-ng-b881500084z |accessdate=27 March 2020 |date=26 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326163115/https://thewest.com.au/news/coronavirus/west-live-perth-couple-stranded-on-costa-victoria-cruise-ship-where-covid-19-case-confirmed-ng-b881500084z |archive-date=26 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://crew-center.com/costa-victoria-passenger-critical-care-after-testing-positive-covid-19 |title=Costa Victoria passenger in critical care after testing positive for COVID-19 |publisher=Crew Center |date=2020-03-24 |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref>

=== {{anchor|Artania|MV Artania}} ''Artania'' ===  <!-- 2020.03.26: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:MV Artania in Trondheim.jpg|thumb|''Artania'' in 2011]]

It was announced on 26 March 2020 that seven passengers on {{ship|MV|Artania}}, moored off the coast of [[Western Australia]], had tested positive for coronavirus.<ref>{{cite web | title=Coronavirus update: Seven WA Artania cruise ship passengers test positive | website=7NEWS.com.au | date=2020-03-26 | url=https://7news.com.au/lifestyle/health-wellbeing/artania-cruise-ship-passengers-test-positive-for-coronavirus-c-763541 | access-date=2020-04-25}}</ref> The ship docked at [[Fremantle Harbour|Fremantle]] in Western Australia on 27 March. Most of the 850 passengers flew home from [[Perth]] to Germany on 28–29 March. 41 passengers and crew tested positive to COVID-19 and are being treated in Perth hospitals.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://apnews.com/2c7aac9cd9ac8d6d78f599a5f218d06b |title=Australia prepares to fly cruise passengers to Germany |agency=Associated Press |date=27 March 2020 |access-date=29 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200328203735/https://apnews.com/2c7aac9cd9ac8d6d78f599a5f218d06b |archive-date=28 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="ABC-30-3-2020">{{cite news|url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-29/confirmed-coronavirus-cases-on-artania-cruise-ship-top-41/12101342|title=Coronavirus patients from Artania cruise ship sent to Joondalup hospital after 29 new COVID-19 positive tests|newspaper=[[ABC News (Australia)]]|date=30 March 2020|accessdate=1 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200401063505/https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-29/confirmed-coronavirus-cases-on-artania-cruise-ship-top-41/12101342|archive-date=1 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> On 1 April, the ship had 450 crew and about a dozen passengers on board. The Australian Government directed ''Artania'' to leave port, but the ship demanded to stay another 14 days, presumably so that they could be treated if COVID-19 symptoms developed.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-04-01/coronavirus-cruise-ship-artania-refusing-to-leave-fremantle-port/12110206|title=Coronavirus cruise ship Artania refuses to leave WA port of Fremantle in letter to Australian Border Force|newspaper=[[ABC News (Australia)]]|date=1 April 2020|accessdate=1 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200401025756/https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-04-01/coronavirus-cruise-ship-artania-refusing-to-leave-fremantle-port/12110206|archive-date=1 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> According to the [[Attorney-General for Australia|Australian Attorney-General]], [[Christian Porter]], "there are still 12 passengers on board some of whom are very unwell. And their level of either illness or frailty is such that they cannot get in a plane."<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.youngwitness.com.au/story/6707149/unwell-on-covid-infected-cruise-ship-in-wa/?cs=9397|title=Unwell on COVID-infected cruise ship in WA|newspaper=The Young Witness|date=1 April 2020|accessdate=1 April 2020}}</ref>

The ''Artania'' left Fremantle on 18 April.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Perpitch |first1=Nicolas |title=Artania cruise ship leaves Fremantle after fatal COVID-19 outbreak amid three more WA coronavirus cases |url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-04-18/artania-cruise-ship-leaves-fremantle-after-coronavirus-outbreak/12161296 |accessdate=18 April 2020 |work=ABC News |publisher=Australian Broadcasting Corporation |date=18 April 2020 |ref=abc-artania-leaves |language=en-AU}}</ref>  The cruise line stated that it was travelling back to Germany with eight passengers aboard.<ref name="artania.cbs">{{cite web|url=https://www.cbs58.com/news/last-ship-belonging-to-a-major-cruise-line-finally-reaches-port |title=Last ship belonging to a major cruise line finally reaches port |publisher=Cbs58.com |date=2020-04-21 |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref>  It was first scheduled to stop at [[Bali]], Indonesia, on 23 April 2020, and [[Manila]], Philippines, on 28 April 2020, to drop some crew members home before heading to [[Bremerhaven]], Germany, with a [[skeleton crew]] of 75 crew members, and arriving around 31 May 2020.<ref name="artania.cbs" /><ref name="artania.industry">[https://www.cruiseindustrynews.com/cruise-news/22813-artania-returns-via-southeast-asia.html Artania Returns Via Southeast Asia] Cruise Industry News 20 April 2020</ref><!-- cruise line statements should stay here instead of appearing at the end of the section, as the statements were made before the ship stopped near jakarta, at which point it was likely that the previously-stated itinerary would not be strictly adhered to, as mentioned in one of the footnotes in the paragraph about jakarta -->

On 23 April, a German man in his 70s, who was a former passenger of ''Artania'', died in [[Perth]] at [[Sir Charles Gairdner Hospital]], marking the fourth death linked to ''Artania''.<ref name="artania.perth" /><ref name="artania.abc.2">{{cite web|url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-04-24/artania-passenger-dies-from-coronavirus-in-perth-hospital/12180868|title=WA coronavirus death toll rises to eight as fourth person from Artania cruise ship dies in hospital – ABC News|date=24 April 2020|website=www.abc.net.au}}</ref>

On 24 April 2020, 57{{efn|Earlier reports stated that 56 crew members had left the ship.<ref name="artania.medcom" /><ref name="artania.republika" />}} Indonesian crew members came ashore at [[Port of Tanjung Priok]], [[North Jakarta]], and were taken to the emergency [[field hospital]] set up at [[Kemayoran Athletes Village]] to be tested for the virus and monitored for 14 days.{{efn|Despite earlier reports that ''Artania'' was going to stop at Bali, apparently no reports have been made of such a stop, so it is assumed that the itinerary changed and Jakarta became the Indonesian stop.  In addition, all reports of ''Artania'' stopping at Jakarta do not explicitly mention that the cruise ship itself had docked, so it is presumed that it anchored near the port and crew members were transported by other means to the port, especially since one source mentions that there was a pickup team from {{ill|TNI Angkatan Laut III|id|Pangkalan Utama TNI Angkatan Laut III}}, an Indonesian naval base.<ref name="artania.medcom" /><ref name="artania.republika" />|name="artania.jakarta"}}<ref name="artania.medcom">{{cite web|url=https://www.medcom.id/nasional/peristiwa/JKRGWRyN-56-abk-mv-artania-dibawa-ke-wisma-atlet |title=56 ABK MV Artania Dibawa ke Wisma Atlet |publisher=Medcom.id |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref><ref name="artania.republika">{{cite web|url=https://republika.co.id/berita/q9aatk428/56-wni-abk-mv-artania-akan-diobservasi-di-rsd-wisma-atlet |title=56 WNI ABK MV Artania akan Diobservasi di RSD Wisma Atlet &#124; Republika Online |publisher=Republika.co.id |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref><ref name="artania.tribun">{{cite web|url=https://jakarta.tribunnews.com/2020/04/24/8-dari-57-wni-abk-mv-artania-positif-corona-dari-hasil-rapid-test|title=8 dari 57 WNI ABK MV Artania Positif Corona dari Hasil Rapid Test|website=Tribun Jakarta}}</ref>  Later that day, [[Yudo Margono]], Commander of Indonesia's {{ill|Joint Regional Defense Command I|id|Komando Gabungan Wilayah Pertahanan I}}, announced that 8 of the crew members had tested positive, while the other 49 members tested negative.<ref name="artania.tribun" />

It is likely that 8 passengers and 346{{efn|One source reported that 411 people were aboard when ''Artania'' left Fremantle, and another reported that there were 8 passengers at the time.<ref name="artania.abc" /><ref name="artania.cbs" />  Subsequently, another source stated that 57 crew members had been taken to an emergency hospital in Jakarta.<ref name="artania.tribun" />|name="artania.crew.2"}} crew members were still on board when ''Artania'' left Indonesian waters.<ref name="artania.cbs" /><ref name="artania.tribun" />  It arrived in [[Manila Bay]] around 30 April, where 236 crew members disembarked before the ship left the bay later on 1 May.{{efn|The ship was located off the coast of Manila along with a number of other cruise ships, including ''Sun Princess'', ''Costa Venezia'', and ''Carnival Spirit'', and stayed in the area for roughly a day before heading out of [[Manila Bay]].<ref name="mapper.2020.04.29">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruisemapper.com/|archive-url=https://archive.today/20200429225244/https://www.cruisemapper.com/?imo=8201480|url-status=dead |archive-date=2020-04-29|title=Cruise Ship Tracker, Itineraries, Schedules, Deck Plans|website=CruiseMapper}}</ref><ref name="mapper.2020.05.01">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruisemapper.com/|archive-url=https://archive.today/20200501210951/https://www.cruisemapper.com/?imo=8201480|archive-date=2020-05-01|url-status=dead|title=Cruise Ship Tracker, Itineraries, Schedules, Deck Plans|website=CruiseMapper}}</ref>  It is unclear if the ship actually docked at Manila or not.}}<ref name="mapper.2020.04.29" /><ref name="artania.sukf">[https://www.schiffe-und-kreuzfahrten.de/news/ms-artania-ausschiffung-236-crewmitgliedern-in-manila-via-singapur-nach-bremerhaven/203199/ MS Artania: Ausschiffung 236 Crewmitgliedern in Manila – via Singapur nach Bremerhaven] Sciffe und Kreuzfahrten</ref><ref name="artania.phoenix">{{cite web|url=https://www.phoenixreisen.com/hier-ist-die-artania-heute-.html|title=Hier befindet sich MS Artania heute|website=www.phoenixreisen.com}}</ref>

''Artania'' arrived at its home port of [[Bremerhaven]] with its last eight passengers on 2020.06.08.{{r|artania.tricks}}{{r|artania.sukf.2}}

=== ''Celebrity Apex'' === <!-- 2020.03.26: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File: Celebrity APEX at Saint Nazaire Jan 2020.jpg|thumb|''Celebrity Apex'' being built at [[Chantiers de l'Atlantique]]]]

On 26 March 2020, the [[Regional Health Agency]] of the [[Regions of France|French region]] [[Pays de la Loire]] reported that seven crew members aboard {{ship||Celebrity Apex||2}} had tested positive for coronavirus.<ref name="apex.ars">{{in lang|fr}} {{cite web |url=https://www.pays-de-la-loire.ars.sante.fr/system/files/2020-03/03-26%20confinement%20Celebrity%20appex%20%282%29.pdf |title= Confinement info |website=www.pays-de-la-loire.ars.sante.fr |access-date=25 April 2020}}</ref>  At the time, ''Celebrity Apex'' was docked at [[Chantiers de l'Atlantique]] in [[Saint-Nazaire]], where it had been built, and was waiting to be delivered to [[Celebrity Cruises]].<ref name="apex.seatrade.1">{{cite web | title=No illness on CMV's Vasco da Gama but ship ordered to 14-day isolation | website=seatrade-cruise.com | date=26 March 2020 | url=https://www.seatrade-cruise.com/news/march-26-updates-celebrity-apex-crew-test-positive-sick-costa-crew-evacuated-vasco-da-gama | access-date=25 April 2020}}</ref>  There were 1407 crew members already on board at the time.<ref name="apex.ars" />

Before the first positive cases were reported, practices aboard ''Celebrity Apex'' did not reflect the seriousness of the progression of the pandemic at the time.<ref name="apex.seatrade.1" />  For example, a large party was held on 21 March 2020, even though the whole country of France had been under lockdown since 17 March 2020, four days earlier.<ref name="apex.seatrade.1" /><ref name="lockdown.france">{{cite web|author=Text by: FRANCE 24 Follow |url=https://www.france24.com/en/20200317-french-lockdown-comes-into-force-in-bid-to-curtail-spread-of-deadly-virus |title=French lockdown comes into force in bid to curtail spread of deadly virus |publisher=France24.com |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref>  However, once the first seven crew members tested positive, the whole crew was placed in isolation and forbidden to leave the ship.<ref name="apex.ars" />

The next day, on 27 March 2020, the ship was delivered virtually to Celebrity Cruises in what was believed to be the first virtual delivery of a cruise ship, necessitated due to the pandemic and the [[travel restrictions related to the COVID-19 pandemic|travel restrictions]] that were in place.<ref name="apex.trade">{{cite web | title=Celebrity Cruises takes delivery of Apex in virtual ceremony | website=Cruise Trade News | date=30 March 2020 | url=https://www.cruisetradenews.com/celebrity-cruises-takes-delivery-celebrity-apex-virtual-ceremony/ | access-date=25 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="apex.youtube">{{cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=knAOVXUgUT0 |title=The Delivery of Celebrity Apex |publisher=YouTube |date=2020-04-01 |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref>  That night, it was reported that 29 people had tested positive for the virus, and one person had been brought to a hospital with breathing issues.<ref name="apex.seatrade.2">{{cite web | title=Celebrity takes virtual delivery of Apex, signals first sailing May 20 | website=seatrade-cruise.com | date=28 March 2020 | url=https://www.seatrade-cruise.com/news/celebrity-takes-virtual-delivery-apex-signals-first-sailing-may-20 | access-date=25 April 2020}}</ref>

By 31 March 2020, 157 persons had tested positive and 2 had been hospitalized;<ref name="apex.bleu">{{cite web|url=https://www.francebleu.fr/infos/sante-sciences/coronavirus-157-membres-de-l-equipage-du-paquebot-celebrity-apex-testes-positifs-1585670064 |title=Coronavirus : 157 occupants du paquebot Celebrity Apex testés positifs |publisher=Francebleu.fr |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref> by the next week, on 7 April 2020, 217 persons had tested positive, with 4 hospitalized and 2 in [[intensive care medicine|intensive care]];<ref name="apex.seatrade.3">{{cite web | title=Ruby Princess docks for crew health assessments | website=seatrade-cruise.com | date=7 April 2020 | url=https://www.seatrade-cruise.com/news/april-7-updates-ruby-princess-and-celebrity-apex-crew-screenings-coral-princess-charters-disney | access-date=25 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="apex.actu">{{cite web|url=https://actu.fr/pays-de-la-loire/saint-nazaire_44184/coronavirus-217-personnes-positives-sur-celebrity-apex-saint-nazaire_32861126.html |title=Coronavirus : 217 personnes positives sur le Celebrity Apex à Saint-Nazaire &#124; L'Écho de la Presqu'île |publisher=Actu.fr |date=2020-04-07 |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref> and by the following week, on 15 April 2020, 224 persons had tested positive, out of a total of 1444 people tested.{{efn|Some sources state that approximately 350 persons had tested positive, but they all seem to have based that number on a lawsuit brought against Celebrity Cruises, where the complaint, filed on 14 April 2020, alleged that on 6 April, <blockquote>[a]pproximately three hundred and fifty (350) crewmembers working aboard the ''Celebrity Apex'' test[ed] positive for COVID-19.  Eight (8) crewmembers who tested positive were admitted to a local French hospital; four (4) such crewmembers <u>who displayed symptoms</u> return[ed] to the ship a few days later, the other four (4) remain[ed] in the French hospital.<ref name="apex.complaint">{{cite web |url=https://www.classaction.org/media/nedeltcheva-v-celebrity-cruises-inc.pdf |title= Celebrity cruises|website= www.classaction.org|access-date=25 April 2020}}</ref></blockquote>  This estimate of roughly 350 crew members testing positive by 2020.04.06 appears much larger than the 217 positive cases that the [[Regional Health Agency]] reportedly reported the following day, so it is assumed to be a very rough estimate.<ref name="apex.actu" />|name="apex.350"}}<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.20minutes.fr/societe/2761143-20200415-coronavirus-saint-nazaire-trois-semaines-plus-tard-encore-700-membres-equipage-apex-rapatrier |title=Coronavirus à Saint-Nazaire : Trois semaines plus tard, encore 700 membres d'équipage de l'" Apex " à rapatrier |publisher=20minutes.fr |date=15 April 2020 |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref>

Because of how Celebrity Cruises treated the crew of ''Celebrity Apex'' during the pandemic, a crew member of ''Celebrity Apex'', who tested positive for the virus on 30 March 2020, filed a [[class action]] lawsuit against the cruise line on 14 April 2020 "on behalf of all ... similarly situated crewmembers working aboard [Celebrity Cruise's] vessels."<ref name="apex.360">{{cite web|url=https://www.law360.com/articles/1263768/celebrity-cruises-hit-with-covid-19-class-suit-by-worker |title=Celebrity Cruises Hit With COVID-19 Class Suit By Worker |publisher=Law360 |accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="apex.herald">{{cite web | last1=Hong | first1=Jae C. | last2=Harris | first2=Alex | title='They absolutely did not care': Crew members sue Celebrity Cruises over virus response | website=miamiherald | date=14 April 2020 | url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/business/tourism-cruises/article242005711.html | access-date=25 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="apex.complaint" />  The lawsuit alleged that Celebrity Cruises failed to provide proper [[personal protective equipment]] (PPE), allowed independent contractors to freely enter and exit the ship, failed to test people boarding the ship for symptoms of coronavirus, failed to enact appropriate lockdown measures, and failed to provide "prompt, proper, and adequate medical care" to its employees, amongst other claims.<ref name="apex.complaint" />

=== ''Costa Favolosa'' === <!-- 2020.03.26: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
{{ship||Costa Favolosa}} departed from Guadeloupe. Six of the disembarked occupants of the ship were tested positive for COVID-19.<ref name="Costa_fox" /> On 26 March, as the ship stopped three miles offshore from Miami, the U.S. Coast Guard reported evacuation of seven sick crew member, out of 1,009 who stayed aboard.<ref name="Costa_nbc" /><ref name="Costa_usatoday" /><ref name="Costa_fox" /> On 8 April 2020 an Indian crew member died from the disease after being hospitalised in a Miami Hospital on 29 March.<ref name="favolosa.usatoday">[https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/04/07/coronavirus-costa-favolosa-crew-member-dies-coral-princess-disembarks/2959938001/ More Coral Princess cruisers leave ship; Costa Favolosa crew member dies of coronavirus] USA Today 7 April 2020</ref>

=== ''MSC Splendida'' === <!-- 2020.03.26: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->

On 23 March 2020, around 14:00 [[Central European Time|CET]], a Thai crew member working aboard {{ship||MSC Splendida}} as a buffet attendant was [[medical evacuation|medically evacuated]] via lifeboat after she exhibited symptoms consistent with the coronavirus disease and was having difficulty breathing.{{efn|She had been suffering from a fever and a sore throat for three days, and her health had been worsening.<ref name="splendida.crew" />}}<ref name="splendida.crew">[https://crew-center.com/msc-splendida-emergency-medical-evacuation-crew-member MSC Splendida Emergency Medical Evacuation of Crew Member  ] CrewCenter 24 March 2020</ref>  At the time, the ship was near the island of [[Sardinia]] and headed to [[Marseille]]{{efn|The cruise originally was supposed to end at [[Genoa]] on 29 March 2020, but the trip was cut short and the end of the cruise was moved up to 24 March when it docked at Marseille.<ref name="splendida.travel">[https://www.travelweekly.co.uk/articles/364103/coronavirus-msc-cruises-promises-to-repatriate-splendida-passengers Coronavirus: MSC Cruises promises to repatriate Splendida passengers] Travel Weekly 20 March 2020</ref>}} to disembark all of its passengers.<ref name="splendida.crew" />{{efn|MSC Cruises stated on 19 March 2020 that there were 1721 passengers aboard,<ref name="splendida.travel" /> while another source stated that, at one point, around 800 were supposed to be disembarking at Marseille, with the wording leaving it being possibly ambiguous as to whether this was referring to the number of passengers or crew.<ref name="splendida.crew" />  In addition, it is unclear if any passengers disembarked during the five days before the ship docked at Marseille.}}

On 24 March 2020, MSC Cruises informed the crew that the sick crew member had tested negative.<ref name="splendida.crew" />  However, two days later, on 26 March, it was reported that the sick crew member had been tested again, and this time, the test had returned positive.<ref name="splendida.crew" />  As a result, 16 crew members were placed under quarantine.<ref name="splendida.crew" />  The ship later docked in [[Genoa]] so that some of its crew members could disembark.<ref name="splendida.abscbn">[https://news.abs-cbn.com/news/04/04/20/more-than-300-filipino-seafarers-from-italy-portugal-back-in-the-philippines More than 300 Filipino seafarers from Italy, Portugal back in the Philippines] ABS News 4 April 2020</ref>

By 1 April 2020, 26 crew members had been placed under quarantine, with 3 crew members running high temperatures.<ref name="splendida.crew" />

=== ''Sun Princess'' === <!-- 2020.03.26: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->

Princess Cruises ship ''Sun Princess'' was not allowed to dock at a port in [[Madagascar]] on 13 February 2020, as it had visited Thailand less than 14 days before. The ship docked at the French island of [[Réunion]] on 1 March, but passengers were met by a crowd of about 30 who insisted that the passengers be tested and tried to prevent them from leaving the port area. Objects were thrown at passengers, and the police deployed tear gas. Princess Cruises said that there was no evidence of SARS-CoV-2 on the ship.<ref name=sun/>

On 26 March 2020, the [[Department of Health (Western Australia)|Department of Health]] of [[Western Australia]] announced that a passenger from ''Sun Princess'' had tested positive for the virus.{{efn|Technically, the [[Department of Health (Western Australia)|Department of Health]]'s announcement on 26 March stated that "four [people who tested positive] are passengers from cruise ships including the Ruby Princess, Sun Princess and Voyager of the Seas", so there may have been two passengers from ''Sun Princess'' who tested positive by this date.<ref name="sun.health" />|name="sun.positive"}}<ref name="sun.health">{{cite web|url=https://ww2.health.wa.gov.au/Media-releases/2020/COVID19-update-26-March-2020 |title=COVID-19 update – 26 March 2020 |publisher=Ww2.health.wa.gov.au |date=2020-03-26 |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref>

=== {{anchor|Zaandam|MS Zaandam|Rotterdam|MS Rotterdam}} ''Zaandam'' and ''Rotterdam'' ===  <!-- 2020.03.27: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->

The [[Holland America Line|Holland America]] cruise ship {{MS|Zaandam}}<!-- standard is to include a ship prefix the first time it is mentioned in the section devoted to the ship if the ship's own wikipedia page mentions the prefix in the preface, and to omit the prefix in all other instances --> was stranded off the coast of Chile after being denied entry to ports from 14 March. Of the 1,829 people (1,243 passengers, 586 crew) aboard, 13 passengers and 29 crew members fell ill with "flu-like symptoms".<ref name="Zaandam_CBC_1">{{cite news |url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/business/cruise-ship-holland-america-covid-19-canadians-1.5506674 |title='Get us the hell off': Canadians on board stranded cruise ship with 42 sick passengers, crew |last=Harris |first=Sophia |work=CBC News |date=23 March 2020 |access-date=23 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200323210317/https://www.cbc.ca/news/business/cruise-ship-holland-america-covid-19-canadians-1.5506674 |archive-date=23 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> The vessel sailed for [[Port Everglades, Florida]], U.S., hoping to dock on 30 March with a total of 77 sick persons aboard as of 24 March.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/business/tourism-cruises/article241457871.html |title=A cruise ship with 77 sick on board hopes to dock in Port Everglades on March 30 |work=Miami Herald |last=Dolven |first=Taylor |date=24 March 2020 |access-date=24 March 2020 passengers died while waiting for permission to transit the [[Panama Canal]], while the number of sick aboard climbed to 148.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bradenton.com/news/coronavirus/article241559956.html |last=Harris |first=Alex |title=Four passengers died on Zaandam cruise ship with 148 people sick with flu-like symptoms |archive-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> Two passengers tested positive for [[COVID-19]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/business/zaandam-cruise-ship-passengers-holland-america-deaths-1.5512490 |title=4 passengers die on stranded cruise ship carrying 247 Canadians |work=CBC News |last=Harris |first=Sophia |date=27 March 2020 |access-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live}}</ref> However, on 27 March, the ship was denied transit through the Panama Canal due to the number of sick people on board.<ref>{{cite web |work=Prensa Latina |date=27 March 2020 |access-date=27 March 2020 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 28 March 2020, both ''Zaandam'' and the accompanying vessel {{MS|Rotterdam||2}} were cleared by the Panama Department of Health to transit through the Panama Canal towards their destination in Florida.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/28/covid-19-holland-america-splitting-up-its-healthy-sick-passengers/2933381001/ |title=Coronavirus: Holland America's Zaandam, Rotterdam get permission to transit Panama Canal |work=USA Today |date=28 March 2020 |access-date=28 March 2020 |archive-date=29 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>  Asymptomatic passengers and some medical staff were transferred from ''Zaandam'' to ''Rotterdam'' while they were both anchored {{convert|8|mi|spell=in|order=flip}} offshore on 28 March. 53 guests and 85 crew members aboard ''Zaandam'' reported flu-like symptoms.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-52072703?intlink_from_url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world/latin_america&link_location=live-reporting-story |title=Coronavirus: Cruise ship off Panama coast transfers passengers |work=BBC News |date=29 March 2020 |access-date=30 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200405090223/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-52072703?intlink_from_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bbc.com%2Fnews%2Fworld%2Flatin_america&link_location=live-reporting-story |archive-date=5 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> By 31 March 2020, the number reported as being "ill" had increased to 193.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/business/covid-19-zaandam-cruise-ship-ill-stranded-1.5515811 |title=More COVID-19 cases on stranded cruise ship with 4 dead. Cruise line pleads for help |date=31 March 2020 |work=Canadian Broadcasting Corporation |access-date=31 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200331095439/https://www.cbc.ca/news/business/covid-19-zaandam-cruise-ship-ill-stranded-1.5515811 |archive-date=31 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

''Rotterdam'' followed ''Zaandam'' on its way to Florida. An unstated number of passengers from ''Zaandam'' were transferred to the second vessel on 28 March 2020.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/28/covid-19-holland-america-splitting-up-its-healthy-sick-passengers/2933381001/ |title=Coronavirus: Holland America's Zaandam, Rotterdam get OK to transit Panama Canal for Florida |last=Hines |first=Morgan |date=28 March 2020 |work=USA Today |access-date=30 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200330022237/https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2020/03/28/covid-19-holland-america-splitting-up-its-healthy-sick-passengers/2933381001/ |archive-date=30 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/30/us/zaandam-cruise-ship-sick-passengers/index.html |title=A cruise ship headed to Florida has reported more sick people on board after 4 die and 2 test positive for Covid-19 |date=30 March 2020 |work=CNN |last=Silverman |first=Hollie |access-date=30 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200330083610/https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/30/us/zaandam-cruise-ship-sick-passengers/index.html |archive-date=30 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> At that time, the crew of ''Zaandam'' included four physicians and four nurses while ''Rotterdam'' had two physicians and four nurses.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.thestar.com/news/canada/2020/03/28/passengers-on-cruise-ship-in-panama-transferred-to-new-vessel.html |title=Passengers on cruise ship in Panama transferred to new vessel |date=28 March 2020 |last=Winsa |first=Patty |work=Toronto Star |access-date=30 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200330054951/https://www.thestar.com/news/canada/2020/03/28/passengers-on-cruise-ship-in-panama-transferred-to-new-vessel.html |archive-date=30 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

As of 30 March 2020, Holland America had not received permission to dock either vessel at Port Everglades in Fort Lauderdale as planned. According to an [[Associated Press]] report, the city's mayor, Dean Trantalis, "said he didn't want the ship to dock near his city, at least without extensive precautions".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.wfla.com/community/health/coronavirus/authority-stranded-ships-begin-transiting-panama-canal/ |title=Authority: Stranded ships begin transiting Panama Canal |date=30 March 2020 |agency=Associated Press |work=WFLA News Channel 8 |access-date=30 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200331153439/https://www.wfla.com/community/health/coronavirus/authority-stranded-ships-begin-transiting-panama-canal/ |archive-date=31 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name=nealdolven>{{cite web |url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/coronavirus/article241605286.html |title=Fort Lauderdale mayor not ready to accept the coronavirus-hit Zaandam at Port Everglades |date=30 March 2020 |last1=Neal |first1=David J. |last2=Dolven |first2=Taylor |name-list-style=amp |work=Miami Herald |access-date=30 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406070837/https://www.miamiherald.com/news/coronavirus/article241605286.html |archive-date=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> The governor of Florida was also hesitant to accept ''Zaandam'' at Fort Lauderdale because the state already had so much to deal with during the pandemic; as of 31 March 2020, a decision had not yet been made. The president of Holland America made a public plea for acceptance of the ship and expressed concern that various ports in several countries had been reluctant to provide provisions and medical supplies.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/business/covid-19-zaandam-cruise-ship-ill-stranded-1.5515811 |title=More COVID-19 cases on stranded cruise ship with 4 dead. Cruise line pleads for help |date=31 March 2020 |work=CBC News |access-date=31 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200331095439/https://www.cbc.ca/news/business/covid-19-zaandam-cruise-ship-ill-stranded-1.5515811 |archive-date=31 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

President Donald Trump said on 1 April 2020 that "we have to help the people" [on the ships] and that discussions were underway about [[Canada]] and the [[United Kingdom]] "arranging flights to retrieve their citizens from the ship". News reports on 2 April stated that the ships would be allowed to dock at Port Everglades that afternoon. The cruise line was making arrangements for passengers who were fit to travel to their home countries to leave via chartered aircraft, directly from the ship to bus and then to airplane.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/cruise-ship-sick-passengers-sister-ship-will-be-allowed-dock-n1174796 |title=Cruise ship with sick passengers and sister ship will be allowed to dock in Florida |last=Burke |first=Minyvonne |work=NBC News |date=2 April 2020 |access-date=2 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200402162022/https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/cruise-ship-sick-passengers-sister-ship-will-be-allowed-dock-n1174796 |archive-date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> From the 442 passengers on ''Zaandam'' and 808 passengers on ''Rotterdam'' there are 107 passengers and 143 crew from 1,186 crew that had influenza-like symptoms, those who had mild symptoms were quarantined in staterooms, and will be released later. All crew, no matter their condition, must stay on board.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/travel/cruises/news/coronavirus-hit-ships-finally-dock-in-port-everglades/ |title=Coronavirus-hit cruise ships finally permitted to disembark healthy passengers in Florida |first=Katherine |last=Lawrey |date=3 April 2020 |access-date=3 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404142455/https://www.telegraph.co.uk/travel/cruises/news/coronavirus-hit-ships-finally-dock-in-port-everglades/ |archive-date=4 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

A report on 4 April stated that "14 critically ill people" were taken to area hospitals while the others were allowed to disembark when flights to their destinations were available.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bnd.com/news/article241769916.html |title=Another cruise ship with virus victims docks in Florida |work=Belleville News-Democrat |last=Anderson |first=Curt |agency=Associated Press |date=4 April 2020 |access-date=5 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406070847/https://www.bnd.com/news/article241769916.html |archive-date=6 April 2020 |url-status=dead }}</ref>

=== {{anchor|Pullmantur Horizon|Horizon|MV Horizon}} '' Horizon'' === <!-- 2020.03.28: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:Horizon in the Port of La Guaira.jpg|thumb|''Horizon'' in 2013]]

An anonymous crew member of the {{MV|Horizon||2}} reported on 28 March 2020 that a member of the crew had tested positive on 26 March 2020.<ref name="horizon.crew">{{cite web|url=http://crew-center.com/pullmantur-horizon-crew-reports-covid-19-positive-cases-onboard |title=Pullmantur Horizon Crew Reports COVID-19 Positive Cases Onboard |publisher=Crew Center |date=2020-04-04 |accessdate=2020-04-12}}</ref>  With about 250 crew members and contractors aboard, the ship had docked at [[Port Rashid]] in [[Dubai]] on 15 March 2020, and the crew has been isolated and under lockdown since.<ref name="horizon.crew" />

On 20 March 2020, another crew member reported that out of 20 crew members tested, 11 were confirmed positive.<ref name="horizon.crew" />  Another crew member reported on 4 April 2020 that, starting on 2 April 2020, all the crew members were being tested, and on 4 April 2020, results were delivered to crew members individually.<ref name="horizon.crew" />  Almost half or more than half of the crew had tested positive.<ref name="horizon.crew" />

=== ''Oasis of the Seas'' === <!-- 2020.03.29: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
On 29 March 2020, the ''[[Miami Herald]]'' reported that 14 crew members of {{ship||Oasis of the Seas}} had tested positive for coronavirus. At that time, the vessel had been at anchor near Port Miami since mid-March. The passengers had disembarked for flights to their home countries but the ship remained in the area.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/coronavirus/article241598366.html|title=14 crew have COVID-19, Royal Caribbean captain says, after passengers got off in Miami|date=29 March 2020|website=Miami Herald}}</ref> As of 10 April 2020, seven crew members had been taken to nearby hospitals within a week.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Harris|first=Alex|url=https://www.bradenton.com/news/coronavirus/article241922051.html|title=Oasis of the Seas docks at Port Everglades to hospitalize more sick crew members|date=10 April 2020|work=Bradenton Herald|access-date=19 April 2020}}</ref> One member of the crew, a Filipino bartender, died of COVID-19 on 18 April.<ref name="miamiherald-20-4-19">{{Cite news|last=Dolven|first=Taylor|url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/business/tourism-cruises/article242120826.html|title=Royal Caribbean crew member from Oasis of the Seas cruise ship dies in Broward hospital|date=19 April 2020|newspaper=[[Miami Herald]]|access-date=24 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="oasis.daily">{{cite web|url=https://www.nydailynews.com/coronavirus/ny-coronavirus-royal-caribbean-oasis-of-the-seas-bartender-waiter-dead-20200421-y5gqq7uq5bgyljvadvfeukm6de-story.html|title=Two Royal Caribbean Oasis of the Seas crew members die of COVID-19 in two days|first=Theresa|last=Braine|website=nydailynews.com}}</ref>  Another crew member, a 41-year-old Indonesian waiter, died of the disease in a hospital in [[Fort Lauderdale, Florida|Fort Lauderdale]] on 20 April.<ref name="oasis.daily" /><ref name="oasis.law">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/04/articles/disease/another-crew-member-from-oasis-of-the-seas-dies-due-to-covid19/|title=Another Crew Member From Oasis of the Seas Dies Due to COVID19|date=20 April 2020|website=Cruise Law News}}</ref>  A third crew member, a long-term employee who worked in the incinerator room, died in a [[Broward County, Florida|Broward County]] hospital during the morning of 3 May.<ref name="oasis.law.2">{{Cite web |url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/05/articles/disease/third-crew-member-from-the-oasis-of-the-seas-dies-due-to-covid-19/ |title=Third Crew Member from the Oasis of the Seas Dies Due to COVID-19 |work=Cruise Law News |date=3 May 2020 |access-date=4 August 2020}}</ref>

=== ''Liberty of the Seas'' === <!-- 2020.03.30: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[Port of Galveston]] officials confirmed on 30 March 2020 that two crew members of {{ship||Liberty of the Seas}} had tested positive for coronavirus.<ref name="liberty.galvnews.1">{{cite web|url=http://www.galvnews.com/news/free/article_86f5f92d-7792-5520-b8f7-3e1b9742bb19.html |title=Two COVID-19 cases confirmed aboard Liberty of the Seas &#124; Local News &#124; The Daily News |publisher=Galvnews.com |date=2020-03-30 |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref>  One was asymptomatic, and remained in quarantine on board the ship, while the other, who showed visible symptoms, disembarked and was hospitalised in [[Galveston, Texas]].<ref name="liberty.crew">{{cite web|url=http://crew-center.com/two-liberty-seas-crew-members-test-positive-covid-19 |title=Two Liberty of the Seas crew members test positive for COVID-19 |publisher=Crew Center |date=2020-04-02 |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref>  The ship left port on the same day, and returned to port on 15 April 2020 after spending roughly two weeks off the coast of Texas.<ref name="liberty.galvnews.1" /><ref name="liberty.galvnews.2">{{cite web|url=https://www.galvnews.com/news/free/article_57cb37d7-c610-5e8b-97f4-74aaa830e52a.html |title=Liberty of the Seas returns to Galveston from quarantine &#124; Local News &#124; The Daily News |publisher=Galvnews.com |date=2020-04-15 |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref>

=== ''Coral Princess'' === <!-- 2020.04.02: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
News reports in early April 2020 indicated that {{ship||Coral Princess}}, with 1,020 passengers and 878 crew, with some suffering flu-like symptoms, was hoping to be allowed to dock at [[Port Everglades]] in [[Fort Lauderdale]] to allow passengers to disembark. A news item on 2 April 2020 stated that "Passengers have been confined to their rooms...when the company noticed a higher than normal number of flu-like cases on board". Reports then specified that "out of 13 passengers and crew tested for COVID-19 on board the Coral Princess, 12 were positive." Officials in [[Broward County, Florida]], said that a plan was not yet in place to handle the situation.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://news.yahoo.com/coral-princess-cruise-ship-12-183437177.html |title=Coral Princess cruise ship with 12 COVID-19 cases on board hopes to dock in Florida |last=Dolven |first=Taylor |work=Miami Herald |date=2 April 2020 |access-date=3 April 2020 |via=Yahoo News}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/business/canadian-passengers-covid-19-princess-coral-cruise-1.5520023 |title=Canadian passengers on virus-stricken Coral Princess cruise ship worry how they'll get home |work=CBC News |date=3 April 2020 |access-date=3 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403165915/https://www.cbc.ca/news/business/canadian-passengers-covid-19-princess-coral-cruise-1.5520023 |archive-date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

''Coral Princess'' was diverted and finally docked at the [[Port of Miami]] on the afternoon of 4 April with its over 1,000 passengers and 878 crew members. A ''CNN'' report that evening indicated that two passengers had died and some others were ill, including the 12 that had tested positive for COVID-19. Those who were not ill were to disembark when flights to their destinations were available; this was expected to take some days.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/04/04/us/coral-princess-cruise-ship-docks-miami-coronavirus/index.html |title=Coral Princess docks in Miami with 2 dead and several ill of coronavirus, after ports shunned it for days |work=CNN |last1=Hanna |first1=Jason |last2=Alonso |first2=Melissa |date=4 April 2020 |access-date=5 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404230618/https://www.cnn.com/2020/04/04/us/coral-princess-cruise-ship-docks-miami-coronavirus/index.html |archive-date=4 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> A subsequent news report later that evening stated that four passengers were scheduled to be taken to Florida hospitals and added that 67 persons would not be allowed to disembark.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.msn.com/en-us/news/us/after-two-deaths-on-board-coral-princess-cruise-ship-gets-miami-welcome/ar-BB12aMiq |title=After two deaths on board, Coral Princess cruise ship gets Miami welcome |last=Freeman |first=Marc |work=South Florida Sun-Sentinel |date=4 April 2020 |access-date=5 April 2020 |via=MSN News}}</ref>

On 6 April, the death of a third passenger was announced.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.msn.com/en-us/news/us/coral-princess-cruise-passenger-dies-of-coronavirus-after-disembarking-delay-daughter-says/ar-BB12a5w2 |title=Coral Princess cruise passenger dies of coronavirus after disembarking delay, daughter says |agency=USA Today |date=6 April 2020 |access-date=6 April 2020 |work=MSN}}</ref> By that afternoon, 684 passengers had disembarked, those who needed medical care had been taken from the vessel and 274 were still on the ''Coral Princess''. Charter flights had departed to Canada, California, Australia and the United Kingdom; others were expected to leave Florida the next day.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/travel/article/coral-princess-coronavirus-disembarkation/index.html |title=Passengers on the Coral Princess cruise ship are still trying to get home |work=CNN |date=7 April 2020 |access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref>

The vessel left Port Miami on 10 April 2020 with its crew and 13 international passengers who were unable to return to their home countries due to travel restrictions. No destination was revealed but it appeared that the ship would initially remain at sea for a period of quarantine.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://wsvn.com/news/local/miami-dade/coral-princess-departs-portmiami-with-13-passengers-quarantined-crew/ |title=Coral Princess departs PortMiami with 13 passengers, quarantined crew |work=WVSN News |date=10 April 2020 |access-date=10 April 2020}}</ref>

=== ''Disney Wonder'' === <!-- 2020.04.05: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
[[File:Disney Wonder cruise ship in Vancouver.jpg|thumb|''Disney Wonder'' in 2014]]

{{ship||Disney Wonder}} arrived at the Port of San Diego on 19 March 2020, where 1,980 passengers disembarked; there were no reports that any had flu-like symptoms. By 5 April, 38 crew members had reportedly tested positive, according to a report by Cruise Law News, based on discussions with unnamed individuals on the ship. [[Disney Cruise Line]], however, told other news media that none of the crew had tested positive.<ref name="wonder.law">{{cite web |url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/04/articles/disease/thirty-eight-crew-members-on-disney-wonder-reportedly-test-positive-for-covid-19/ |title=Thirty-Eight Crew Members on Disney Wonder Reportedly Test Positive for COVID-19 |date=5 April 2020 |publisher=Cruise Law News |access-date=10 April 2020 }}</ref>

A passenger who disembarked at San Diego on 20 March reported that no health screening activities, such as the asking of health-related questions or the taking of temperatures, occurred upon disembarkation, and that the only health screening that occurred was during the check-in process two weeks prior.<ref name="wonder.law" />

The crew was tested for the virus again in the middle of May, with around 200 crew members testing positive.<ref name="wonder.law.2">{{cite web|url=https://www.cruiselawnews.com/2020/05/articles/disease/around-200-crew-members-on-disney-wonder-reportedly-test-positive-for-covid-19/|title=Around 200 Crew Members on Disney Wonder Reportedly Test Positive for COVID-19|date=19 May 2020|website=Cruise Law News}}</ref>

=== ''Greg Mortimer'' ===  <!-- 2020.04.06: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
== COVID-19 ==  <!-- 2020.04.06: first known report of first positive case, used to order ships chronologically -->
On 7 April 2020, {{ship||Greg Mortimer|ship|2}}, which held 114 passengers, was stranded in Uruguay for a week and asking for help after people exhibited symptoms such as fever, which prompted authorities to ban them from disembarking.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.sbs.com.au/news/greg-mortimer-81-people-test-positive-for-covid-19-on-australian-cruise-ship-off-uruguay |title=Greg Mortimer: 81 people test positive for COVID-19 on Australian cruise ship off Uruguay |work=SBS News |last=Blakkarly |first=Jarni |date=6 April 2020 |access-date=8 April 2020}}</ref> After the Uruguayan medical teams boarded the cruise ship to test passengers, staff and crew on 1 April, 81 people tested positive for [[COVID-19]], with six people being evacuated and transferred to hospitals having become ill with [[COVID-19]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.smh.com.au/national/more-than-80-passengers-on-board-greg-mortimer-cruise-ship-test-positive-for-covid-19-20200406-p54hk4.html |title=More than 80 passengers on board Greg Mortimer cruise ship test positive for COVID-19 |work=The Sydney Morning Herald |last=Noyes |first=Jenny |date=6 April 2020 |access-date=8 April 2020}}</ref>

A news report on 8 April stated that the ship had not yet received permission to dock, although an evacuation flight to Australia and New Zealand was being arranged by Aurora Expeditions. By that time, 128 persons on the vessel had tested positive for COVID-19. Six had been transferred to a hospital in [[Montevideo]]. 

''Greg Mortimer'' was eventually able to dock in Montevideo on 10 April 2020.<ref name="mortimer.reuters">{{cite web | title=Uruguay transports Australians, New Zealanders from virus-hit cruise ship | website=Reuters | date=2020-04-11 | url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirius-uruguay-cruiseshi-idUSKCN21S21M | access-date=2020-04-25}}</ref>  A total of 112 passengers (96 Australians and 16 New Zealanders) were transported via a humanitarian corridor of ambulances and buses to Montevideo's [[Carrasco International Airport]], where they boarded a chartered [[Hi Fly (airline)|Hi Fly]] [[Airbus A340|Airbus A340-300]] flight to [[Australia]]. The direct flight, one of the longest passenger flights ever at a length of roughly 12400 kilometers (6700 [[nautical mile]]s), cost roughly 15000 [[Australian dollar|AUD]] per passenger, as the plane was refitted as a medical plane, had to be flown first from Portugal to Uruguay before flying to Australia and then back to Europe, had to be cleaned extensively following the flight, and required two flight crews.

<ref name="mortimer.sbs">{{cite web|last=Kwan |first=Biwa |url=https://www.sbs.com.au/news/greg-mortimer-australian-new-zealand-passengers-go-into-quarantine-after-arriving-in-melbourne |title=Greg Mortimer: Australian, New Zealand passengers go into quarantine after arriving in Melbourne &#124; SBS News |publisher=Sbs.com.au |date=2020-04-11 |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref><ref name="mortimer.update">{{cite web|url=https://www.auroraexpeditions.com.au/asg80-update/ |archive-url=https://archive.today/20200409142048/https://www.auroraexpeditions.com.au/asg80-update/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=2020-04-09 |title=Current Voyage Update &#124; Aurora Expeditions™ |publisher=Archive.is |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref><ref name="hi.fly">{{cite web|url=https://www.instagram.com/p/B-4OxSLBCuL/ |title=Hi Fly on Instagram: "Hi Fly A340 registration 9H-SUN makes history flying 16h16m from Montevideo to Melbourne, a route of 6700 nm repatriating Australians. One…" |publisher=Instagram.com |accessdate=2020-04-25}}</ref>  The plane landed in [[Melbourne]] early on 12 April, and all passengers subsequently entered a 14-day quarantine in a hotel.<ref name="mortimer.sbs" />

Two Australians remained in Uruguay as they remained in intensive care at a hospital.<ref name="mortimer.reuters" />  Passengers of other nationalities also remained on board the ship pending negotiations with their home countries.<ref name="mortimer.reuters" />


A news report on 8 April stated that the ship had not yet received permission to dock, although an evacuation flight to Australia and New Zealand was being arranged by Uruguayan authorities. By that time, 128 persons on the vessel had tested positive for COVID-19. Six had been transferred to a hospital in [[Montevideo]]. Passengers from Europe and America who had positive tests would not be allowed to travel to their home countries until their subsequent tests indicated negative results.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/04/07/americas/greg-mortimer-cruise-ship-coronavirus-intl-hnk/index.html |title=Passengers to be evacuated from Antarctic cruise ship after almost 60% test positive for coronavirus |date=8 April 2020 |work=CNN |last1=Griffiths |first1=James |last2=Castillo |first2=Jackie |name-list-style=amp |access-date=8 April 2020 }}</ref>

''Greg Mortimer'' was eventually able to dock in Montevideo on 10 April 2020.<ref name="mortimer.reuters">{{cite web | title=Uruguay transports Australians, New Zealanders from virus-hit cruise ship | website=Reuters | date=2020-04-11 | url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirius-uruguay-cruiseshi-idUSKCN21S21M | access-date=2020-04-25}}</ref>  A total of 112 passengers (96 Australians and 16 New Zealanders) were transported via a humanitarian corridor of ambulances and buses to Montevideo's [[Carrasco International Airport]], where they boarded a chartered [[Hi Fly (airline)|Hi Fly]] [[Airbus A340|Airbus A340-300]] flight to [[Australia]].{{efn|The direct flight, one of the longest passenger flights ever at a length of roughly 12400 kilometers (6700 [[nautical mile]]s), cost roughly 15000 [[Australian dollar|AUD]] per passenger, as the plane was refitted as a medical plane, had to be flown first from Portugal to Uruguay before flying to Australia and then back to Europe, had to be cleaned extensively following the flight, and required two flight crews.<ref name="mortimer.update" /><ref name="hi.fly" />}}<ref>
